Self-Tazkiyah: The Witness Impugning Himself
Ruling on self-impugnment with moral dimension

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a witness's self-impugnment and identify the sin involved.

Core Idea
A witness's statement that he is unjust is a valid admission against himself, but he sins if truthful.

What happens when a witness declares himself unreliable? The Hanafi school treats this as a binding admission, but also warns of sin. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the moral dimension from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act: a witness says he is not just (ghayr adl). Ruling: this is accepted as an admission (iqrar) that disqualifies him.
The text says 'is an admission against himself, binding upon him.'
2
Understand the moral consequence
If the witness is truthful in his self-impugnment, he sins because he causes the plaintiff's right to be lost.
Al-Zahiriyya is cited: 'he sins by that if he is truthful in his testimony because it involves invalidating the plaintiff's right.'
3
Contrast with self-praise
Self-praise (saying 'I am just') is not accepted as tazkiyah; only self-impugnment is effective.
The text earlier hinted that self-tazkiyah is like opponent's tazkiyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه آخر: يسأل القاضي عن الشهود الذمة عدول المسلمين وإلا فيسأل عنهم عدول الكفار؛ كذا في المحيط والاختيار. قوله: ( وتعديل الخصم لا يصح) أي تزكية المدعى عليه الشاهد بقوله هو عدل غير مقبولة لأن في زعم المدعي وشهوده أن الخصم كاذب في إنكاره مبطل في إصراره فلا يصلح معدلاً. وموضوع المسألة إذا قال عدول إلا أنهم أخطؤوا أو نسوا، أما إذا قال صدقوا أو هم عدول صدقة فقد اعترف بالحق؛ كذا في الهداية. وفي شرح أدب القضاء للصدر الشهيد أن يكون مقراً بقوله صدقوا فيما شهدوا به علي وبقوله هم عدول فيما شهدوا به علي. أطلقه وقيده في البزازية بما إذا كان المدعى عليه لا يرجع إليه في التعديل فإن كان صح قوله. وشمل الخصم المدعي والمدعى عليه وإن أراد به المدعى عليه وهو الظاهر فعدم صحته من المدعي بأولى كتعديل الشاهد نفسه. وأما فمقبول لما في البزازية: وقول الشاهد إنه ليس بعدل إقراره على نفسه جائز عليه وكان ينبغي له أن لا يفعل ا هـ. وظاهر ما في الظهيرية أنه يأثم بذلك حيث كان صادقاً في شهادته لما فيه من إبطال حق المدعي. ولم يذكر المؤلف رحمه الله تعديل أحد الشاهدين صاحبه وفيه اختلاف؛ قال في الظهيرية: شاهدان شهدا لرجل والقاضي يعرف أحدهما بالعدالة ولا يعرف الآخر فعدله الذي عرفه القاضي بالعدالة. قال نصير رحمه الله: لا يقبل القاضي تعديله ولابن سلمة فيه قولان، وعن أبي بكر البلخي في ثلاثة شهدوا والقاضي يعرف اثنين منهم بالعدالة ولا يعرف الثالث فإن القاضي يقبل تعديلهما لو شهد هذا الثالث شهادة أخرى ولا يقبل تعديلهما في الشهادة الأولى وهو كما قال نصير رحمه الله تعالى ا هـ. وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا عدله المدعى عليه قبل الشهادة أو بعدها كما في البزازية ويحتاج إلى تأمل فإنه قبل الدعوى لم يوجد منه كذب في إنكاره وقت التعديل وكان الفسق الطارئ على المعدل قبل القضاء كالمقارن. وفي البزازية: ولا يسأل رجلاً له على المشهود عليه دين فلسه الحاكم. وهذا دليل على أن الشاهد إذا كان له دين على المشهود عليه وهو مفلس لا تقبل اهـ. وفي المحيط البرهاني من دفع الدعاوى معزياً إلى الأوزجندي: إذا قال المدعى عليه بعد الشهادة لي دفع لا يكون تعديلاً للشهود الجواز أن يكون بالطعن في الشاهد اهـ. قلت: بخلاف قول المدعي عليه في جواب دعوى الوكيل بالدين دفعته إلى الموكل أو أبرأني فإنه يكون إقراراً بالوكالة فإنه يؤمر بالدفع إلى الوكيل كما سيأتي فيها. قوله: (والواحد يكفي للتزكية والرسالة والترجمة وهذا عندهما. وقال محمد: لا يجوز
Another note: The judge asks about the witnesses of the dhimma (non-Muslim subjects) from just Muslims, otherwise he asks about them from just disbelievers; thus in al-Muhit and al-Ikhtiyar. His statement: (And the adjustment of the opponent is not valid) meaning the defendant's tazkiyah of the witness by saying 'he is just' is not acceptable, because in the claim of the plaintiff and his witnesses, the opponent is a liar in his denial and wrong in his persistence, so he is not suitable as a modifier. The subject of the issue is when he says 'they are just except that they erred or forgot', but if he says 'they spoke truth' or 'they are just, believe them', then he has confessed the right; thus in al-Hidaya. In Sharh Adab al-Qada' by al-Sadr al-Shahid, he must be confessing by his statement 'they spoke truth in what they testified against me' and by his statement 'they are just in what they testified against me'. It was left unrestricted and restricted in al-Bazzaziyya to when the defendant is not relied upon for tazkiyah; if he is, his statement is accepted. And it includes the opponent whether plaintiff or defendant, though he meant the defendant, which is apparent, so its lack of validity from the plaintiff is even more so, like tazkiyah of the witness by himself. And as for [self-tazkiyah], it is accepted because of what is in al-Bazzaziyya: The witness's statement that he is not just is an admission against himself, binding upon him, and he should not do it. End quote. And the apparent from al-Zahiriyya is that he sins by that if he is truthful in his testimony because it involves invalidating the plaintiff's right. And the author (may Allah have mercy on him) did not mention the adjustment of one of the two witnesses by his companion, and there is disagreement about it. He said in al-Zahiriyya: Two witnesses testified for a man, and the judge knows one of them to be just, but does not know the other, so the one he knows to be just adjusts him. Nasir (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The judge does not accept his adjustment. And Ibn Salama has two opinions. And from Abu Bakr al-Balkhi regarding three who testified, and the judge knows two of them to be just and does not know the third: the judge accepts the adjustment of the two if this third testifies in another case, but does not accept their adjustment in the first testimony. And it is as Nasir (may Allah have mercy on him) said. End quote. And he left it unrestricted, so it includes whether the defendant adjusted him before or after the testimony, as in al-Bazzaziyya. And it needs reflection, for before the lawsuit, there was no lie from him in his denial at the time of adjustment, and the sin that occurs on the part of the modifier before the judgment is like that which coexists. In al-Bazzaziyya: And the judge does not ask a man who has a debt on the one against whom testimony is given if he is insolvent. This is evidence that if a witness has a debt on the one against whom he testifies and he is insolvent, his testimony is not accepted. End quote. In al-Muhit al-Burhani from Daf' al-Da'awa quoting al-Awzjandi: If the defendant after testimony says 'I have a defense', it is not an adjustment of the witnesses because it could be impugning the witness. End quote. I say: Unlike the defendant's statement in answer to the agent's claim of debt, 'I paid it to the principal' or 'he discharged me', for that is an acknowledgment of the agency, so he is ordered to pay the agent as will come later. His statement: (And one suffices for tazkiyah, message, and translation, and this is according to them both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And Muhammad said: It is not permissible...
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This final passage of the window delves into several specific issues within the law of testimony, each with its own legal reasoning (ta'lil). First, regarding tazkiyah by the opponent (al-khasm): The text rules that a defendant's statement that a witness is just is not acceptable as tazkiyah. The reason given is that the defendant's position inherently contradicts the plaintiff's claim; by denying the claim, the defendant implicitly accuses the witnesses of lying, so his word cannot be trusted to exalt their credibility. However, if the defendant explicitly says 'they spoke the truth' or 'they are just, believe them', that is considered an admission of liability, not a tazkiyah. The Hidayah is cited for this distinction. Al-Sadr al-Shahid's commentary adds that the defendant must be effectively confessing to the claim when he endorses the witnesses. Al-Bazzaziyya qualifies that if the defendant is not the one relied upon for tazkiyah (i.e., he is not a credible source even when not a party), then his adjustment of the witness is invalid anyway. The same reasoning applies a fortiori to the plaintiff (who is also a party) and to self-tazkiyah (a witness declaring himself just). On self-tazkiyah, the text cites al-Bazzaziyya that if a witness declares himself unjust, that is a valid admission against himself, and he should not do so. Al-Zahiriyya adds that he sins by such self-impugnment if he is truthful, because it invalidates the plaintiff's right. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq then notes that the matn author (al-Kanz) did not mention the issue of one witness adjusting his fellow witness. The text records a dispute: In al-Zahiriyya, Nasir says the judge does not accept such adjustment, while Ibn Salama has two opinions. Abu Bakr al-Balkhi makes a distinction: if the known just witnesses vouch for the third in a separate case, it is accepted; but in the same case, it is not. The text also addresses the situation where a witness has a debt on the opposing party and that party is insolvent—such testimony is not accepted because of perceived bias. Finally, the text touches on the rule that one single person suffices for tazkiyah, for delivering a message (risala), and for translation (tarjama). This is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two companions), while Imam Muhammad is reported to have said it is not permissible (probably referring to tazkiyah by one; the text cuts off). This intra-Hanafi dispute is left partially unresolved, but the relied-upon position is that one person is sufficient for tazkiyah, as is well known in the school.

Key Terms
جرح الشاهد نفسه (jarh al-shahid nafsahu): Self-impugnment: a witness declaring himself unjust, which is a valid admission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the moral ruling on a witness who truthfully impugns himself?
A) He is rewarded for honesty.
B) He commits a sin because he invalidates the plaintiff's right.
C) He is neutral; no reward or sin.
D) He is punished for lying if he is actually just.

Key Takeaway
A witness's self-impugnment is legally accepted as an admission but morally sinful if true.

Shahadat — Testimony

One Witness Adjusting Another: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on one witness adjusting another

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the intra-Hanafi disagreement on a known just witness adjusting his fellow witness, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Whether a known just witness can adjust his companion is disputed; some accept in separate cases, others never.

When a judge knows one witness to be just, can that witness vouch for the other? The Hanafi school has conflicting views. This lesson explores the positions of al-Nasir, Ibn Salama, and Abu Bakr al-Balkhi, and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the problem
Two witnesses testify; the judge knows one to be just, the other not. The known just witness says the other is just.
This is the scenario from al-Zahiriyya.
2
Identify the positions
Al-Nasir: the judge does not accept. Ibn Salama: two opinions. Abu Bakr al-Balkhi: distinguishes between the same case and a different case.
The text says: 'Nasir said: the judge does not accept his adjustment. Ibn Salama has two opinions. Abu Bakr al-Balkhi: in a separate case accepted, in the same case not.'
3
Analyze the reasoning
The concern is circularity: if a witness adjusts his companion in the same case, it creates a conflict of interest. But in a different case, the link is weaker.
No explicit dalil given; reasoning is based on practice and avoiding circularity.
4
Determine the thamarah
Practical consequence: some Hanafi judges accept the adjustment in a separate case; others do not accept it at all.
Author does not give definitive tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This final passage of the window delves into several specific issues within the law of testimony, each with its own legal reasoning (ta'lil). First, regarding tazkiyah by the opponent (al-khasm): The text rules that a defendant's statement that a witness is just is not acceptable as tazkiyah. The reason given is that the defendant's position inherently contradicts the plaintiff's claim; by denying the claim, the defendant implicitly accuses the witnesses of lying, so his word cannot be trusted to exalt their credibility. However, if the defendant explicitly says 'they spoke the truth' or 'they are just, believe them', that is considered an admission of liability, not a tazkiyah. The Hidayah is cited for this distinction. Al-Sadr al-Shahid's commentary adds that the defendant must be effectively confessing to the claim when he endorses the witnesses. Al-Bazzaziyya qualifies that if the defendant is not the one relied upon for tazkiyah (i.e., he is not a credible source even when not a party), then his adjustment of the witness is invalid anyway. The same reasoning applies a fortiori to the plaintiff (who is also a party) and to self-tazkiyah (a witness declaring himself just). On self-tazkiyah, the text cites al-Bazzaziyya that if a witness declares himself unjust, that is a valid admission against himself, and he should not do so. Al-Zahiriyya adds that he sins by such self-impugnment if he is truthful, because it invalidates the plaintiff's right. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq then notes that the matn author (al-Kanz) did not mention the issue of one witness adjusting his fellow witness. The text records a dispute: In al-Zahiriyya, Nasir says the judge does not accept such adjustment, while Ibn Salama has two opinions. Abu Bakr al-Balkhi makes a distinction: if the known just witnesses vouch for the third in a separate case, it is accepted; but in the same case, it is not. The text also addresses the situation where a witness has a debt on the opposing party and that party is insolvent—such testimony is not accepted because of perceived bias. Finally, the text touches on the rule that one single person suffices for tazkiyah, for delivering a message (risala), and for translation (tarjama). This is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two companions), while Imam Muhammad is reported to have said it is not permissible (probably referring to tazkiyah by one; the text cuts off). This intra-Hanafi dispute is left partially unresolved, but the relied-upon position is that one person is sufficient for tazkiyah, as is well known in the school.

Key Terms
تعديل أحد الشاهدين صاحبه (ta'dil ahad al-shahidayn sahibahu): The adjustment of one witness by his fellow witness in the same case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Bakr al-Balkhi, when is the adjustment of a third witness by two known just witnesses accepted?
A) In the same case only.
B) In a different case only.
C) Always accepted.
D) Never accepted.

Key Takeaway
The adjustment of one witness by another is an unresolved intra-Hanafi dispute with practical consequences.

The Rule of One Person Suffices for Tazkiyah, Message, and Translation
Ruling on sufficiency of one modifier

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that one person suffices for tazkiyah, and identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement with Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
One person suffices for tazkiyah, message delivery, and translation according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Is one modifier enough to establish witness probity? The majority of the Hanafi school says yes, based on practice. This lesson presents the ruling and the dissenting view of Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
The text says: 'And one suffices for tazkiyah, message, and translation. This is according to them both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani).'
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the dissenter
Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani is reported to have said: 'It is not permissible.'
The text cuts off but the meaning is clear.
3
Understand the basis
The majority view is based on practice and necessity; the dissenting view may require two witnesses as in other testimonies.
No explicit dalil is given in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه آخر: يسأل القاضي عن الشهود الذمة عدول المسلمين وإلا فيسأل عنهم عدول الكفار؛ كذا في المحيط والاختيار. قوله: ( وتعديل الخصم لا يصح) أي تزكية المدعى عليه الشاهد بقوله هو عدل غير مقبولة لأن في زعم المدعي وشهوده أن الخصم كاذب في إنكاره مبطل في إصراره فلا يصلح معدلاً. وموضوع المسألة إذا قال عدول إلا أنهم أخطؤوا أو نسوا، أما إذا قال صدقوا أو هم عدول صدقة فقد اعترف بالحق؛ كذا في الهداية. وفي شرح أدب القضاء للصدر الشهيد أن يكون مقراً بقوله صدقوا فيما شهدوا به علي وبقوله هم عدول فيما شهدوا به علي. أطلقه وقيده في البزازية بما إذا كان المدعى عليه لا يرجع إليه في التعديل فإن كان صح قوله. وشمل الخصم المدعي والمدعى عليه وإن أراد به المدعى عليه وهو الظاهر فعدم صحته من المدعي بأولى كتعديل الشاهد نفسه. وأما فمقبول لما في البزازية: وقول الشاهد إنه ليس بعدل إقراره على نفسه جائز عليه وكان ينبغي له أن لا يفعل ا هـ. وظاهر ما في الظهيرية أنه يأثم بذلك حيث كان صادقاً في شهادته لما فيه من إبطال حق المدعي. ولم يذكر المؤلف رحمه الله تعديل أحد الشاهدين صاحبه وفيه اختلاف؛ قال في الظهيرية: شاهدان شهدا لرجل والقاضي يعرف أحدهما بالعدالة ولا يعرف الآخر فعدله الذي عرفه القاضي بالعدالة. قال نصير رحمه الله: لا يقبل القاضي تعديله ولابن سلمة فيه قولان، وعن أبي بكر البلخي في ثلاثة شهدوا والقاضي يعرف اثنين منهم بالعدالة ولا يعرف الثالث فإن القاضي يقبل تعديلهما لو شهد هذا الثالث شهادة أخرى ولا يقبل تعديلهما في الشهادة الأولى وهو كما قال نصير رحمه الله تعالى ا هـ. وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا عدله المدعى عليه قبل الشهادة أو بعدها كما في البزازية ويحتاج إلى تأمل فإنه قبل الدعوى لم يوجد منه كذب في إنكاره وقت التعديل وكان الفسق الطارئ على المعدل قبل القضاء كالمقارن. وفي البزازية: ولا يسأل رجلاً له على المشهود عليه دين فلسه الحاكم. وهذا دليل على أن الشاهد إذا كان له دين على المشهود عليه وهو مفلس لا تقبل اهـ. وفي المحيط البرهاني من دفع الدعاوى معزياً إلى الأوزجندي: إذا قال المدعى عليه بعد الشهادة لي دفع لا يكون تعديلاً للشهود الجواز أن يكون بالطعن في الشاهد اهـ. قلت: بخلاف قول المدعي عليه في جواب دعوى الوكيل بالدين دفعته إلى الموكل أو أبرأني فإنه يكون إقراراً بالوكالة فإنه يؤمر بالدفع إلى الوكيل كما سيأتي فيها. قوله: (والواحد يكفي للتزكية والرسالة والترجمة وهذا عندهما. وقال محمد: لا يجوز
Another note: The judge asks about the witnesses of the dhimma (non-Muslim subjects) from just Muslims, otherwise he asks about them from just disbelievers; thus in al-Muhit and al-Ikhtiyar. His statement: (And the adjustment of the opponent is not valid) meaning the defendant's tazkiyah of the witness by saying 'he is just' is not acceptable, because in the claim of the plaintiff and his witnesses, the opponent is a liar in his denial and wrong in his persistence, so he is not suitable as a modifier. The subject of the issue is when he says 'they are just except that they erred or forgot', but if he says 'they spoke truth' or 'they are just, believe them', then he has confessed the right; thus in al-Hidaya. In Sharh Adab al-Qada' by al-Sadr al-Shahid, he must be confessing by his statement 'they spoke truth in what they testified against me' and by his statement 'they are just in what they testified against me'. It was left unrestricted and restricted in al-Bazzaziyya to when the defendant is not relied upon for tazkiyah; if he is, his statement is accepted. And it includes the opponent whether plaintiff or defendant, though he meant the defendant, which is apparent, so its lack of validity from the plaintiff is even more so, like tazkiyah of the witness by himself. And as for [self-tazkiyah], it is accepted because of what is in al-Bazzaziyya: The witness's statement that he is not just is an admission against himself, binding upon him, and he should not do it. End quote. And the apparent from al-Zahiriyya is that he sins by that if he is truthful in his testimony because it involves invalidating the plaintiff's right. And the author (may Allah have mercy on him) did not mention the adjustment of one of the two witnesses by his companion, and there is disagreement about it. He said in al-Zahiriyya: Two witnesses testified for a man, and the judge knows one of them to be just, but does not know the other, so the one he knows to be just adjusts him. Nasir (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The judge does not accept his adjustment. And Ibn Salama has two opinions. And from Abu Bakr al-Balkhi regarding three who testified, and the judge knows two of them to be just and does not know the third: the judge accepts the adjustment of the two if this third testifies in another case, but does not accept their adjustment in the first testimony. And it is as Nasir (may Allah have mercy on him) said. End quote. And he left it unrestricted, so it includes whether the defendant adjusted him before or after the testimony, as in al-Bazzaziyya. And it needs reflection, for before the lawsuit, there was no lie from him in his denial at the time of adjustment, and the sin that occurs on the part of the modifier before the judgment is like that which coexists. In al-Bazzaziyya: And the judge does not ask a man who has a debt on the one against whom testimony is given if he is insolvent. This is evidence that if a witness has a debt on the one against whom he testifies and he is insolvent, his testimony is not accepted. End quote. In al-Muhit al-Burhani from Daf' al-Da'awa quoting al-Awzjandi: If the defendant after testimony says 'I have a defense', it is not an adjustment of the witnesses because it could be impugning the witness. End quote. I say: Unlike the defendant's statement in answer to the agent's claim of debt, 'I paid it to the principal' or 'he discharged me', for that is an acknowledgment of the agency, so he is ordered to pay the agent as will come later. His statement: (And one suffices for tazkiyah, message, and translation, and this is according to them both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And Muhammad said: It is not permissible...
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This final passage of the window delves into several specific issues within the law of testimony, each with its own legal reasoning (ta'lil). First, regarding tazkiyah by the opponent (al-khasm): The text rules that a defendant's statement that a witness is just is not acceptable as tazkiyah. The reason given is that the defendant's position inherently contradicts the plaintiff's claim; by denying the claim, the defendant implicitly accuses the witnesses of lying, so his word cannot be trusted to exalt their credibility. However, if the defendant explicitly says 'they spoke the truth' or 'they are just, believe them', that is considered an admission of liability, not a tazkiyah. The Hidayah is cited for this distinction. Al-Sadr al-Shahid's commentary adds that the defendant must be effectively confessing to the claim when he endorses the witnesses. Al-Bazzaziyya qualifies that if the defendant is not the one relied upon for tazkiyah (i.e., he is not a credible source even when not a party), then his adjustment of the witness is invalid anyway. The same reasoning applies a fortiori to the plaintiff (who is also a party) and to self-tazkiyah (a witness declaring himself just). On self-tazkiyah, the text cites al-Bazzaziyya that if a witness declares himself unjust, that is a valid admission against himself, and he should not do so. Al-Zahiriyya adds that he sins by such self-impugnment if he is truthful, because it invalidates the plaintiff's right. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq then notes that the matn author (al-Kanz) did not mention the issue of one witness adjusting his fellow witness. The text records a dispute: In al-Zahiriyya, Nasir says the judge does not accept such adjustment, while Ibn Salama has two opinions. Abu Bakr al-Balkhi makes a distinction: if the known just witnesses vouch for the third in a separate case, it is accepted; but in the same case, it is not. The text also addresses the situation where a witness has a debt on the opposing party and that party is insolvent—such testimony is not accepted because of perceived bias. Finally, the text touches on the rule that one single person suffices for tazkiyah, for delivering a message (risala), and for translation (tarjama). This is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two companions), while Imam Muhammad is reported to have said it is not permissible (probably referring to tazkiyah by one; the text cuts off). This intra-Hanafi dispute is left partially unresolved, but the relied-upon position is that one person is sufficient for tazkiyah, as is well known in the school.

Key Terms
الواحد يكفي للتزكية (al-wahid yakfi li al-tazkiyah): One person suffices to establish the probity of a witness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who among the early Hanafi masters is reported to disagree that one person suffices for tazkiyah?
A) Abu Hanifa
B) Abu Yusuf
C) Muhammad al-Shaybani
D) Imam Muhammad (the imam himself)

Key Takeaway
The majority Hanafi view accepts one person for tazkiyah, message, and translation, while Imam Muhammad dissents.

Ruling on the Judge Translating Testimony
States the ruling when the judge knows the witness's language

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a judge understands the witness's language and explain why a single translator is not permissible.

Core Idea
When the judge knows the language, a single translator’s testimony is impermissible — the judge must hear directly.

This lesson focuses on a key procedural ruling in Hanafi testimony (shahada). The commentator on Kanz al-Daqāʾiq clarifies that if the judge himself understands the language of the witness and the opposing party, he cannot accept testimony through a single translator. The passage also offers lexical definitions of 'tarjama' (translation) and 'tazkiyah' (commendation) to ground the ruling in precise terminology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The judge must be knowledgeable of the language of both the witness and the litigant. This is the condition that triggers the ruling.
If the judge lacks knowledge of even one, the ruling may not apply.
2
State the ruling
When the condition is met, the translation of a single person (tarjamat al-wāhid) is not permissible (lā tajūz).
The term 'lā tajūz' indicates a legal prohibition.
3
Understand the rationale
The judge can hear directly, so a translator's report is unnecessary and introduces potential uncertainty. A single translator's account is akin to hearsay.
This is consistent with the Hanafi emphasis on direct testimony.
4
Note the lexical definitions
The commentator defines 'tarjama' as expressing speech in another language, and 'tazkiyah' as commendation or praise of a witness's character.
These definitions are from al-Miṣbāḥ and al-Ṣiḥāḥ, respectively.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ظاهره أن القاضي إذا كان عارفاً بلسان الشاهد والخصم لم تجز ترجمة الواحد. وفي المصباح : ترجم فلان كلامه إذا بينه وأوضحه، وترجم كلام غيره إذا عبر عنه بلغة غير لغة المتكلم واسم الفاعل ترجمان وفيه لغات أجودها فتح التاء وضم الجيم ، والثانية ضمهما معاً وتجعل التاء تابعة للجيم والثالثة فتحهما بجعل الجيم تابعة للتاء والجمع تراجم ا هـ . والتزكية المدح. قال في الصحاح : زكى نفسه تزكية مدحها ا هـ .
It is apparent that if the judge is knowledgeable of the language of the witness and the litigant, the translation of a single person is not permissible. In al-Misbah: 'So-and-so translated his speech' means he explained and clarified it, and 'translated the speech of another' means he expressed it in a language other than the speaker's language. The active noun is turjumān, and there are variant pronunciations, the best being with fatḥa on tā' and ḍamma on jīm; second, both with ḍamma making the tā' follow the jīm; third, both with fatḥa making the jīm follow the tā'. The plural is tarājim. End quote. And al-tazkiyah is praise. In al-Ṣiḥāḥ: 'He praised (zakkā) himself' meaning he commended himself. End quote.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the commentator on the matn of Kanz al-Daqā'iq regarding the translation of testimony. The default ruling (ẓāhiruh) is that when the judge himself understands the language of the witness and the opposing party, he cannot rely on a single translator. The reason is that when the judge is capable of direct understanding, the need for a translator is eliminated; a single translator's testimony would be akin to hearsay without full confirmation. The commentator then cites al-Miṣbāḥ to define the term 'tarjama' (translation) and its linguistic forms. He also defines 'tazkiyah' (commendation of a witness) as praise, from the root zakā, meaning to commend. This is not the place for a detailed ruling but rather a terminological clarification supporting the main ruling.

Key Terms
ترجمة (tarjama): To express speech in another language as defined in al-Miṣbāḥ
تزكية (tazkiyah): Praise or commendation of a witness's character

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the judge knows Arabic and the witness testifies in Arabic, can he accept the testimony via a single translator?
A) Yes
B) No
C) Only if the translator is upright
D) Only if two translators

Key Takeaway
A judge who understands the witness's language must hear testimony directly; a single translator's account is not permissible.

Four Witnesses Exempt from Judicial Inquiry
Enumerates four witness types exempt from judicial questioning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four exceptions to judicial questioning of witnesses in Hanafi fiqh and explain the rationale for each.

Core Idea
Four witness types are exempt from initial questioning due to special circumstances.

The judge's duty to inquire into witness credibility is a cornerstone of Islamic court procedure. However, Hanafi fiqh recognizes four exceptional cases where this inquiry is waived. This lesson examines those exceptions and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
The base text states that the judge asks about witnesses' integrity. This establishes the default rule of judicial inquiry.
The rule is from Kanz al-Daqā'iq.
2
List the Four Exceptions
Memorize the four types: shāhid al-ṭīnah, shāhid ta'dīl al-'alāniyah, shāhid al-gharīb, and shāhid al-'adwā.
3
Understand Each Exception's Context
For each type, identify the scenario that triggers the exemption. For example, shāhid al-ṭīnah involves an absent defendant's refusal to appear; shāhid al-gharīb involves a stranger's urgent claim.
The rationale often involves necessity or public knowledge.
4
Recognize the Source
The exceptions are transmitted from Ismā'īl ibn Ḥammād, the grandson of Abū Ḥanīfah, a respected scholar who studied under Abū Yūsuf.
His authority is significant in the Hanafi school.
5
Apply the Exceptions
In practice, when a witness falls into one of these categories, the judge may proceed without preliminary questioning. This facilitates justice in special circumstances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه : يستثنى من قوله أولاً وسأل عن الشهود أربعة شهود لا يسأل القاضي عنهم : في أدب القضاء قال إسماعيل بن حماد أربعة من الشهود لا أسأل شاهد الطينة، وشاهد تعديل العلانية، وشاهد الغريب ليدعوه القاضي على غير قرعة، وشاهد العدوى. وشرحها في شرحي منظومة ابن وهبان من أول الشهادات، وإسماعيل هذا هو حفيد أبي حنيفة وهو من جملة الأئمة أخذ عن أبي يوسف وزاحمه في العلم ولو عمر لفاق المتقدمين ولكنه مات شاباً .
A note: An exception is made from his earlier statement 'and he asks about the witnesses' — four witnesses the judge does not ask about. In Adab al-Qaḍā', Ismā'īl ibn Ḥammād said: Four witnesses I do not ask about: the witness of the clay seal (shāhid al-ṭīnah), the witness of open commendation (shāhid ta'dīl al-'alāniyah), the witness of the stranger (shāhid al-gharīb) for the judge to call him without casting lots, and the witness of contagious disease (shāhid al-'adwā). Their explanation is in my two commentaries on the poem of Ibn Wahbān from the beginning of the Book of Testimonies. This Ismā'īl is the grandson of Abū Ḥanīfah and is among the imams; he studied under Abū Yūsuf and competed with him in knowledge; if he had lived longer he would have surpassed the predecessors, but he died young.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is a note (tanbīh) from the commentator enumerating four types of witnesses whom the judge is not required to question regarding their integrity ('adālah). These are exceptions to the general rule that the judge should investigate witnesses. The first is the witness of the clay seal (shāhid al-ṭīnah), which refers to a case where a litigant claims a debt from an absent person and the judge gives him a clay seal or ring to present to the absent party as a summons; if the absent party refuses to appear, witnesses to that refusal are not questioned. The second is the witness of open commendation (shāhid ta'dīl al-'alāniyah), where witnesses testify to a person's uprightness publicly; their own integrity is presumed because the commendation itself is public and well-known. The third is the witness of the stranger (shāhid al-gharīb), where a foreigner claims urgency and needs a quick hearing; the judge may call him without casting lots and the witnesses to his claim are not questioned regarding their 'adālah due to the exigency. The fourth is the witness of contagious disease (shāhid al-'adwā), which is a case where a person identifies a communicable disease in an animal or property and the witnesses to that identification are not questioned. The commentator also provides a brief biography of Ismā'īl ibn Ḥammād, the grandson of Abū Ḥanīfah, noting his scholarly standing.

Key Terms
شاهد الطينة (shāhid al-ṭīnah): Witness to the refusal of an absent person to appear when summoned via clay seal
شاهد تعديل العلانية (shāhid ta'dīl al-'alāniyah): Witness to public commendation of another's character
شاهد الغريب (shāhid al-gharīb): Witness for a stranger who claims urgency and needs immediate hearing
شاهد العدوى (shāhid al-'adwā): Witness to contagious disease or defect in property

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is one of the four types of witnesses the judge does not ask about?
A) Witness to a contract
B) Witness of the clay seal (shāhid al-ṭīnah)
C) Witness to a will
D) Witness to divorce

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school identifies four exceptional witnesses whose involvement in specific circumstances exempts them from the usual judicial inquiry into their credibility.

Condition of 'Adālah in the One Who Gives Tazkiyah
Critical refinement of the condition of 'adālah in the muzaakki

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of 'adālah for the muzaakki and explain why the judge does not question the muzaakki's own uprightness.

Core Idea
The muzaakki must be 'ādil and known to the judge; his tazkiyah is testimony requiring uprightness.

You may wonder: if the judge does not ask the muzaakki about his own character, does that mean 'adālah is unnecessary for him? A serious misunderstanding arose from this silence. The commentator clarifies the true Hanafi position and refutes the error with consensus and textual proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the general Hanafi ruling: the muzaakki (one who commends a witness's character) must possess 'adālah (uprightness).
This is the established position in the Hanafi school.
2
Analyze the Misunderstanding
Examine why Ibn al-Shiḥnah thought 'adālah was not required: because the judge does not ask the muzaakki about his own character, one might think his uprightness is irrelevant.
The judge's silence could be misinterpreted as a lack of condition.
3
Trace the Correction
Understand the commentator's refutation: the reason the judge does not ask is that the muzaakki is already known to be 'ādil. If not known, his tazkiyah is rejected.
The muzaakki's known uprightness is a prerequisite, not a result of questioning.
4
Examine the Proof (Ijma)
The commentator cites transmitted consensus: 'open tazkiyah is like testimony.' Testimony requires 'adālah, so tazkiyah does as well.
This ijma is the decisive dalil.
5
Apply the Correct Understanding
Conclude that the mufta bihi is: the muzaakki must be 'ādil and known to the judge; otherwise his tazkiyah is invalid. The view of Qāḍī Ismā'īl is weak unless secret tazkiyah preceded.
This avoids the confusion between public and secret tazkiyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قلت : فيحتاج هنا إلى فهم قولهم لا بد من العدالة في المزكي فإنه لا يسأل عنه فتعين أن يكون المراد بالمزكي العدل من كان معروفاً بها عند القاضي فإن لم يكن معروفاً بها لم يسأل عنه فلا يقبل تزكيته كما لا يخفى وليس المراد أنه لا يشترط عدالة المزكي كما فهمه العلامة ابن الشحنة بناء على أنها للاحتياط للاكتفاء بتزكية السر لتصريح الكل باشتراط عدالة المزكي خصوصاً في تزكية العلانية وإنما المراد ما فهمناه عنهم، ولما نظر إلى عدم السؤال في المسائل الثلاث لأجل الاكتفاء بالمستور ظن أن المزكي كذلك وليس كما ظنه لما قدمناه من التصريح عنهم وإن كان ما فهمه هو المراد، فما ذكره القاضي إسماعيل ضعيف لنقل الإجماع على أن تزكية العلانية كالشهادة أو هو محمول على ما إذا تقدمت التزكية سراً وهو الظاهر.
I say: So here one needs to understand their statement 'the muzaakki must have 'adālah, for he is not asked about it.' Thus it is determined that what is meant by 'the muzaakki' is the upright person who is known as such to the judge; if he is not known as such, he is not asked about it, so his tazkiyah is not accepted, as is obvious. It does not mean that 'adālah of the muzaakki is not a condition, as understood by 'Allāmah Ibn al-Shiḥnah based on the idea that it is for precautionary reserve and that secret tazkiyah is sufficient, because everyone explicitly states the condition of 'adālah of the muzaakki, especially in open tazkiyah. Rather, what is meant is what we understood from them. And when he considered the lack of questioning in the three cases due to sufficiency of the concealed [witness], he thought the muzaakki is likewise, but it is not as he thought, as we have presented from their explicit statements. Although what he understood is the intended meaning, what Qāḍī Ismā'īl mentioned is weak, due to the transmission of consensus that open tazkiyah is like testimony, or it is interpreted as when secret tazkiyah has preceded, and that is the apparent view.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (taḥqīq) by the commentator regarding the condition of 'adālah (uprightness) in the person who gives tazkiyah (commendation of a witness). The general ruling is that the muzaakki must be 'ādil (upright). However, a misunderstanding arose: because the judge does not ask the muzaakki about his own character, some, like Ibn al-Shiḥnah, thought that the condition of 'adālah is not required for the muzaakki—they thought it is sufficient that the muzaakki is 'mustawr' (of hidden status). The commentator refutes this by clarifying that the reason the judge does not ask is because the muzaakki is already known to be upright. If he is not known, his tazkiyah is not accepted. Furthermore, the commentator argues that the three cases (from the previous exceptions) where questioning is omitted are based on sufficiency of 'mustawr' witnesses, but that does not apply to the muzaakki. He cites transmitted consensus (ijmā') that open tazkiyah is equivalent to testimony, thus requiring the muzaakki to be 'ādil. The view of Qāḍī Ismā'īl is considered weak, or is interpreted as applying only when secret tazkiyah has preceded.

Key Terms
المزكي (al-muzakkī): The person who gives tazkiyah (commendation) of a witness's character.
تزكية العلانية (tazkiyah al-'alāniyah): Open commendation of a witness's character.
المستور (al-mastūr): A person whose character is not openly known but not known to be corrupt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because the muzaakki is assumed to be 'ādil unless proven otherwise
C) Because the muzaakki is already known to be 'ādil to the judge
D) Because the muzaakki must be a 'mustawr'

Key Takeaway
The muzaakki must be 'ādil and known to the judge; the judge's silence is due to prior knowledge, not a waiver of the condition.

When a Witness May Testify: Direct Perception and Exceptions
States the ruling on witness testimony based on direct perception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a witness may testify based on direct perception and list the exceptions where a single just person suffices, including the case of theft nisab valuation.

Core Idea
A witness may testify only to what he personally heard or saw; a single just person suffices in eleven specified matters, but not for theft's nisab.

This lesson explains the foundational rule of witness testimony in Hanafi fiqh: a witness must have direct sensory experience. The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq outlines the general principle and then lists exceptions where a single just person suffices for acting upon information rather than establishing legal proof. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correctly applying the law of evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
Read the opening statement: the witness may testify to what he heard or saw in cases like sale, acknowledgment, judge's ruling, usurpation, and killing, even if not formally summoned.
The key is direct perception – hearing or seeing – not hearsay.
2
List the Eleven Exceptions
The text enumerates eleven matters where a single just person suffices: (1) description of salam item after delivery, (2) insolvency of a prisoner to release him, (3) defect in sold item, (4) sighting crescent of Ramadan, (5) death, (6) purity of water, (7) impurity, (8) permissibility of food, (9) prohibition, (10) dismissal of agent, (11) interdiction of permitted person, etc.
These are matters of information (khabar), not full testimony (shahadah).
3
Understand the Hanafi Principle
Abu Hanifa holds that testimony requires either number (two witnesses) or probity (one witness plus oath). The exceptions are where a single just person is sufficient for acting upon the news, not for establishing a right in court.
This distinguishes legal proof (thubut) from practical action (amal).
4
Apply the Exception to the Exception
The passage notes that in valuation of the nisab of theft, two witnesses are required, not one. This is because the nisab is a fixed quantum and its proof requires the same strictness as the theft itself.
This shows that even in the exceptional category, some matters require extra caution.
5
Analyze the Role of Probity
The text distinguishes between a just person (adl) and a concealed person (mastur). For the eleven matters, a single just person is accepted, but a concealed person is not accepted. Probity is a condition for acceptance in these cases.
In standard testimony, both number and probity are required; here only probity is needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And the letter and the translation? And he may testify to what he heard or saw in the likes of sale, acknowledgment, judge's ruling, usurpation, and killing, even if he was not present as a witness. And he may not testify to another's testimony unless he witnessed it. And the seventh: they differed regarding the description of the salam item after its delivery. The eighth: informing about the insolvency of one imprisoned to release him. The ninth: informing about a defect in the sold item. The tenth: informing about sighting the crescent of Ramadan. The eleventh: informing about death. Then know that this is not exhaustive, because matters of religion accept the word of a single just person, like the purity of water and its impurity, and the permissibility of food and its prohibition, and it is not specific to sighting the crescent of Ramadan. Also, the word of a just person is accepted regarding the dismissal of a agent, the interdiction of a permission, the virgin's notification of her guardian's marriage, the partner's notification of sale, and a Muslim who did not emigrate, and similar, as we presented according to Abu Hanifa regarding the requirement of one of the two conditions of testimony: either number or probity, except that it is said that they did not mention them with it because probity is not a condition for acting upon concealed persons, and the discussion is about where probity is required, so that the news of concealed persons is not accepted in eleven places. Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining when a witness may testify based on direct perception. The core rule: a witness may testify to what he personally heard or saw in cases like sale, acknowledgment, the judge's ruling, usurpation, and intentional killing, even if he was not formally summoned as a witness. The phrase 'including what he heard or saw' indicates that the testimony must be based on direct sensory experience, not hearsay. The passage then lists exceptions where the testimony of a single just person is accepted: informing about salam specifications, insolvency, defects, crescent sighting, and death. However, this list is not exhaustive; other matters like purity and impurity also accept a single just person. Following Abu Hanifa, testimony requires either two witnesses (number) or one witness plus an oath (probity), but in certain cases a single just person suffices for acting upon the information, not for establishing legal proof. The exception to the sufficiency of one in valuation is the valuation of the nisab for theft, which requires two witnesses. This is a well-established rule in the Hanafi school, based on the principle that the nisab is a fixed quantity and its proof requires the same strictness as the act of theft itself.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahādah): Testimony given in court to establish a right or fact; requires number (two witnesses) or probity in the Hanafi school.
عدالة (ʿadālah): Probity, the quality of being just and avoiding major sins and persistent minor sins, required for witnesses in legal testimony.
مستورين (mastūrīn): Persons whose probity is not known but who are not known to be dishonest; their news may be acted upon in certain matters.

Key Takeaway
A witness may testify only to what he personally saw or heard; a single just person suffices for specific religious and practical notifications, but not for theft nisab valuation.

Testifying to Ownership by Purchase and Concealed Witnesses
Ruling on testifying to ownership by purchase vs. absolute ownership, and permissibility of concealed witnesses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that testifying to ownership by purchase requires knowing the price, and explain that a concealed witness may testify if he can see and hear the confessor.

Core Idea
Testimony on ownership by purchase is invalid if the price is unknown; concealed witness testimony is permissible.

In Hanafi fiqh, the conditions for valid testimony depend on the basis of ownership. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies when a witness can testify that someone owns an item by purchase, and when a witness can conceal himself. Understanding these rules ensures that court testimony is precise and just.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of ownership testimony
The witness can testify to ownership by purchase (milk bi al-shira') or absolute ownership (milk mutlaq). The ruling differs based on which basis is chosen.
Absolute ownership is original; purchase is a new event.
2
Determine the condition for testifying by purchase
The price must be known. If the witness does not know the exact price, the testimony is invalid because a sale with an unknown price is void in Hanafi law.
This condition ensures clarity in transactions.
3
Apply the condition to a scenario
If a witness sees a man buy an item but does not know the price, he cannot testify to ownership by purchase. He may testify to absolute ownership if he knows the man owns it from any other basis, or he cannot testify at all.
4
Recognize the permissibility of concealed witnesses
A witness may hide his identity while observing the confessor, as long as he sees and understands him. This is particularly allowed against oppressors. The confessor does not need to know the witness.
Concealed testimony is valid for the sake of justice.
5
Understand the Hanafi preference
The preferred ruling (mufta bihi) is that the witness should specify the basis of ownership rather than use absolute ownership, because absolute ownership is from the origin while purchase is a new event.
The text says 'the first is more correct.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ملك على الشراء لأن الحكم بالشراء بثمن مجهول لا يصح كما في شهادات البزازية. وفي الخلاصة : رجل حضر بيعاً ثم احتيج إلى الشهادة للمشتري ليشهد له بالملك بسبب الشراء ولا يشهد له بالملك المطلق قال : ورأيت في موضع آخر أنه يحل والأول أصح لأن الملك المطلق من الأصل والملك بالشراء حادث ا هـ . وأشار بقوله «وإن لم يشهد عليه» إلى أنه لا يشترط أن يعلم المقر بالشاهد بالأولى فلو اختفى الشاهد وستر نفسه ويرى وجه المقر ويفهمه والمقر لا يعلمه وسعه أن يشهد وهكذا يفعل بالظلمة كما في خزانة الأكمل.
He (the witness) has ownership over the purchase because ruling by a purchase with an unknown price is not valid, as in the Shahadat of al-Bazzaziyyah. And in al-Khulasah: A man witnessed a sale, then there was need for testimony for the buyer that he testifies for him with ownership due to purchase, and he does not testify for him with absolute ownership. He said: I saw in another place that it is permissible, but the first is more correct because absolute ownership is original, and ownership by purchase is incidental. And he indicated by his statement 'and if he does not testify against him' that it is not required that the confessor knows the witness a priori; so if the witness hides and covers himself, and sees the face of the confessor and understands him, and the confessor does not know him, it is permissible for him to testify. And thus it is done with oppressors, as in Khizanat al-Akmal.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement explaining the conditions of testifying to ownership. It distinguishes between testifying that someone owns an item absolutely (ownership from the origin) and testifying that he owns it by purchase. The latter requires knowing the price, otherwise the testimony is invalid as a sale with unknown price is invalid. The preferred opinion is that a witness should specify the basis of ownership. The passage also addresses the case of a concealed witness who hides himself but sees and hears the confessor. This is permissible even if the confessor does not know the witness, and is especially used against oppressors. The authority is from the Khizanat al-Akmal and other Hanafi texts.

Key Terms
ملك مطلق (milk mutlaq): Absolute ownership without specifying the cause (e.g., inheritance, purchase).
شاهد مخفي (shahid mukhfi): A witness who conceals his identity from the opponent but sees and hears him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A witness must know the price to testify to ownership by purchase; concealed witness testimony is valid if the witness sees and hears the confessor.

Testimony on Unknown Weight and Ambiguous Acknowledgment
Ruling on testimony with two illustrative cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for valid testimony when the witness does not know the exact weight or quantity, and apply it to scenarios of ambiguous acknowledgment.

Core Idea
Testimony is valid if the witness has sufficient knowledge to specify the item, even without exact weight.

This lesson examines two examples from Hanafi fatwa works. The first concerns witnesses who saw a purse of dirhams but did not know the exact weight. The second involves a man who acknowledged one of two dirhams (large and small) without specification. Both cases hinge on the requirement that witnesses must have sufficient knowledge of what they testify to. The Hanafi school allows testimony in these situations under specific conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core requirement
Recognize that the witness must know what he testifies to; this is signalled by the phrase 'bima sami'a' (by what he heard).
Knowledge must be direct and sufficient.
2
Apply to the purse scenario
The witnesses saw a purse but did not know the weight. The condition for valid testimony is that they examined the purse and could specify its quantity and quality.
Quality check ensures the dirhams are not defective (e.g., 'stooq').
3
Apply to the ambiguous acknowledgment scenario
A man acknowledged one of two dirhams (large/small) without specifying. The witnesses then heard but did not know which. The ruling orders delivery of the smaller.
This resolves ambiguity by giving the lesser to avoid excess.
4
Derive the principle
Testimony does not require absolute precision; sufficient knowledge and examination suffice. Ambiguity is resolved in favor of the lesser obligation.
This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on practicality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار بقوله «بما سمع إلى أنه لا بد من علم الشاهد بما يشهد به ولهذا قال في النوازل: سئل أبو القاسم عن رجل ادعى على ورثة ميت مالاً فأمر بإثبات ذلك فأحضر شاهدين فشهدا أن المتوفى قد أخذ هذا من المدعي . منديلاً فيه دراهم ولم يعلما كم وزنها أتجوز شهادتهما؟ وهل يجوز للشاهدين أن يشهدا بذلك؟ قال : إن كان الشهود وقفوا على تلك الصرة وفهموا أنها دراهم وحرروها فيما يقع عليه تعيينهم من مقدارها شهدوا بذلك وينبغي أن يعتبرا جودتها فإنها قد تكون ستوقاً فإذا فعلوا ذلك جازت شهادتهم ا هـ . وفي خزانة الأكمل: رجل في یده در همان كبير وصغير قأقر بأحدهما لرجل فشهدا أنه أقر بأحدهما لا ندري بأيهما أقر فإنه يؤمر بتسليم الصغير ا هـ . والإقرار يصح أيضاً أن يكون مثالاً لهما، أما كونه من المسموعات فظاهر، وأما كونه من المرئيات فبالكتاب لما في البزازية من كتاب الإقرار : كتب كتاباً فيه أقر بين يدي الشهود فهذا على أقسام الأول أن يكتب ولا يقول شيئاً وأنه لا يكون إقراراً فلا تحل الشهادة بأنه إقرار قال القاضي النسفي : إن كتب مصدراً مرسوماً وعلم الشاهد حل له الشهادة على إقراره كما لو أقر كذلك وإن لم يقل أشهد علي به . وعلى هذا إذا كتب للغائب على وجه الرسالة أما بعد فلك علي كذا يكون إقراراً لأن الكتاب من الغائب كالخطاب من الحاضر فيكون متكلماً، والعامة على خلافه لأن الكتابة قد تكون للتجربة. وفي حق الأخرس يشترط أن يكون معنوناً مصدراً وإن لم يكن إلى الغائب الثاني كتب وقرأ عند الشهود لهم أن يشهدوا به وإن لم يقل اشهدوا علي الثالث أن يقرأ هذا عندهم غيره فيقول الكاتب اشهدوا علي به الرابع أن يكتب عندهم ويقول اشهدوا علي بما فيه إن علموا بما فيه كان إقراراً وإلا فلا .
And he indicated by his statement 'what he heard' that it is necessary for the witness to know what he testifies to. For this reason it was said in al-Nawazil: Abu al-Qasim was asked about a man who claimed money from the heirs of a deceased, so he ordered its proof. He brought two witnesses who testified that the deceased had taken from the claimant a handkerchief containing dirhams, and they did not know its weight. Is their testimony valid? And is it permissible for the witnesses to testify to that? He said: If the witnesses had observed that purse and understood that it was dirhams, and they examined it to the extent that they could specify its quantity, they should testify to that, and they should consider its quality because it might be 'stooq' (a type of coin?). If they do that, their testimony is valid. And in Khizanat al-Akmal: A man had in his hand a large and a small dirham, and he acknowledged one of them to a man. Then they (witnesses) testified that he acknowledged one of them, but we do not know which one he acknowledged. He will be ordered to deliver the small one. And iqrar (acknowledgment) is also valid to be an example for them (the two categories: audible and visible). As for it being from the audible, it is apparent. As for it being from the visible, it is through writing. For in al-Bazzaziyyah from the book of iqrar: He wrote a book in which he acknowledged before witnesses. This is divided into divisions. First: that he writes and says nothing, and it is not an iqrar, so testimony that it is an iqrar is not permissible. Al-Qadi al-Nasafi said: If he wrote with a formal seal and the witness knew, it is permissible for him to testify to his iqrar, just as if he had acknowledged in that way, even if he did not say 'take witness upon it'. And according to this, if he wrote to an absentee as a letter: 'Amma ba'd, you owe me such-and-such,' it is an iqrar because the writing of an absentee is like the speech of the present, so he becomes a speaker. The general scholars disagree because writing may be for trial. And in the case of a mute, it is required that it be addressed and formal, even if not to the absentee. Second: he writes and reads it to the witnesses, they may testify to it even if he does not say 'take witness upon me'. Third: another person reads it to them, and the writer says 'take witness upon me'. Fourth: he writes in their presence and says 'take witness upon what is in it'; if they know what is in it, it is an iqrar, otherwise not.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, addressing the requirement that a witness must have knowledge of what he testifies to. It gives examples from al-Nawazil and Khizanat al-Akmal. In the first example, witnesses saw a purse of dirhams but did not know the exact weight. The ruling from Abu al-Qasim is that if they examined the purse and could specify the quantity, their testimony is valid, and they should also consider the quality of the coins. In the second example, a man acknowledged one of two dirhams (large and small) without specification; the ruling is that he must deliver the smaller, because the acknowledgment is valid but ambiguous, and the lesser is taken to avoid excess. The passage then discusses iqrar (acknowledgment) as an example of audible and visible matters. It details the categories of written iqrar: a simple writing without spoken statement is not iqrar unless it is sealed and formal according to Qadi al-Nasafi; a letter to an absentee is iqrar according to Nasafi but the general scholars disagree. For a mute, writing is considered speech. The four divisions cover different scenarios of writing and reading. The Hanafi madhhab accepts testimony based on written iqrar under certain conditions.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment of a right or debt; can be audible or visible.
ستوق (stooq): Probably a type of coin or alloy; indicates need to assess quality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if two witnesses saw a deceased take a purse of dirhams from a claimant but did not know its exact weight, can they testify?
A) Yes, without any condition.
B) No, because they must know the exact weight.
C) Yes, if they examined the purse and could specify the quantity and quality.
D) No, because the claimant must bring witnesses who know the weight.

Key Takeaway
Witnesses may testify to what they have sufficient knowledge of, even without exact measurement, as long as they can specify and have examined the matter.

Validity of Written Acknowledgment (Iqrar) in Testimony
Detailed ruling on written iqrar with four divisions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four categories of written iqrar and state the conditions under which written acknowledgment constitutes valid iqrar according to the Hanafi madhhab.

Core Idea
A written iqrar can be as binding as an oral one if it is sealed and witnessed.

This lesson examines the detailed ruling on written iqrar as found in al-Bazzaziyyah. The Hanafi madhhab recognizes that iqrar can be made by writing, but there are divisions based on how the writing is presented to witnesses. The dispute between al-Qadi al-Nasafi and the general scholars regarding a letter to an absentee highlights the need for formality. Understanding these categories is essential for judges and witnesses dealing with documentary evidence.

Guided Path
1
Understand the basis of written iqrar
Iqrar can be either audible (spoken) or visible (written). The written form is valid under specific conditions.
This is a Hanafi position.
2
First division: writing without speech
If a person writes an acknowledgment but says nothing, it is not iqrar unless the writing is sealed and formal according to al-Nasafi.
The 'ammah (general scholars) disagree.
3
Second division: writing and reading to witnesses
If the person writes and reads it to the witnesses, they may testify even without a verbal request to witness.
Reading establishes knowledge.
4
Third and fourth divisions: formal request
If someone else reads and the writer says 'bear witness', or if the writer writes in their presence and says 'bear witness to what is in it', it is iqrar if the witnesses know the content.
Knowledge of content is essential.
5
Special case of the mute
For a mute person, writing is considered equivalent to speech, provided it is formal and addressed.
This accommodates disability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار بقوله «بما سمع إلى أنه لا بد من علم الشاهد بما يشهد به ولهذا قال في النوازل: سئل أبو القاسم عن رجل ادعى على ورثة ميت مالاً فأمر بإثبات ذلك فأحضر شاهدين فشهدا أن المتوفى قد أخذ هذا من المدعي . منديلاً فيه دراهم ولم يعلما كم وزنها أتجوز شهادتهما؟ وهل يجوز للشاهدين أن يشهدا بذلك؟ قال : إن كان الشهود وقفوا على تلك الصرة وفهموا أنها دراهم وحرروها فيما يقع عليه تعيينهم من مقدارها شهدوا بذلك وينبغي أن يعتبرا جودتها فإنها قد تكون ستوقاً فإذا فعلوا ذلك جازت شهادتهم ا هـ . وفي خزانة الأكمل: رجل في یده در همان كبير وصغير قأقر بأحدهما لرجل فشهدا أنه أقر بأحدهما لا ندري بأيهما أقر فإنه يؤمر بتسليم الصغير ا هـ . والإقرار يصح أيضاً أن يكون مثالاً لهما، أما كونه من المسموعات فظاهر، وأما كونه من المرئيات فبالكتاب لما في البزازية من كتاب الإقرار : كتب كتاباً فيه أقر بين يدي الشهود فهذا على أقسام الأول أن يكتب ولا يقول شيئاً وأنه لا يكون إقراراً فلا تحل الشهادة بأنه إقرار قال القاضي النسفي : إن كتب مصدراً مرسوماً وعلم الشاهد حل له الشهادة على إقراره كما لو أقر كذلك وإن لم يقل أشهد علي به . وعلى هذا إذا كتب للغائب على وجه الرسالة أما بعد فلك علي كذا يكون إقراراً لأن الكتاب من الغائب كالخطاب من الحاضر فيكون متكلماً، والعامة على خلافه لأن الكتابة قد تكون للتجربة. وفي حق الأخرس يشترط أن يكون معنوناً مصدراً وإن لم يكن إلى الغائب الثاني كتب وقرأ عند الشهود لهم أن يشهدوا به وإن لم يقل اشهدوا علي الثالث أن يقرأ هذا عندهم غيره فيقول الكاتب اشهدوا علي به الرابع أن يكتب عندهم ويقول اشهدوا علي بما فيه إن علموا بما فيه كان إقراراً وإلا فلا .
And he indicated by his statement 'what he heard' that it is necessary for the witness to know what he testifies to. For this reason it was said in al-Nawazil: Abu al-Qasim was asked about a man who claimed money from the heirs of a deceased, so he ordered its proof. He brought two witnesses who testified that the deceased had taken from the claimant a handkerchief containing dirhams, and they did not know its weight. Is their testimony valid? And is it permissible for the witnesses to testify to that? He said: If the witnesses had observed that purse and understood that it was dirhams, and they examined it to the extent that they could specify its quantity, they should testify to that, and they should consider its quality because it might be 'stooq' (a type of coin?). If they do that, their testimony is valid. And in Khizanat al-Akmal: A man had in his hand a large and a small dirham, and he acknowledged one of them to a man. Then they (witnesses) testified that he acknowledged one of them, but we do not know which one he acknowledged. He will be ordered to deliver the small one. And iqrar (acknowledgment) is also valid to be an example for them (the two categories: audible and visible). As for it being from the audible, it is apparent. As for it being from the visible, it is through writing. For in al-Bazzaziyyah from the book of iqrar: He wrote a book in which he acknowledged before witnesses. This is divided into divisions. First: that he writes and says nothing, and it is not an iqrar, so testimony that it is an iqrar is not permissible. Al-Qadi al-Nasafi said: If he wrote with a formal seal and the witness knew, it is permissible for him to testify to his iqrar, just as if he had acknowledged in that way, even if he did not say 'take witness upon it'. And according to this, if he wrote to an absentee as a letter: 'Amma ba'd, you owe me such-and-such,' it is an iqrar because the writing of an absentee is like the speech of the present, so he becomes a speaker. The general scholars disagree because writing may be for trial. And in the case of a mute, it is required that it be addressed and formal, even if not to the absentee. Second: he writes and reads it to the witnesses, they may testify to it even if he does not say 'take witness upon me'. Third: another person reads it to them, and the writer says 'take witness upon me'. Fourth: he writes in their presence and says 'take witness upon what is in it'; if they know what is in it, it is an iqrar, otherwise not.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, addressing the requirement that a witness must have knowledge of what he testifies to. It gives examples from al-Nawazil and Khizanat al-Akmal. In the first example, witnesses saw a purse of dirhams but did not know the exact weight. The ruling from Abu al-Qasim is that if they examined the purse and could specify the quantity, their testimony is valid, and they should also consider the quality of the coins. In the second example, a man acknowledged one of two dirhams (large and small) without specification; the ruling is that he must deliver the smaller, because the acknowledgment is valid but ambiguous, and the lesser is taken to avoid excess. The passage then discusses iqrar (acknowledgment) as an example of audible and visible matters. It details the categories of written iqrar: a simple writing without spoken statement is not iqrar unless it is sealed and formal according to Qadi al-Nasafi; a letter to an absentee is iqrar according to Nasafi but the general scholars disagree. For a mute, writing is considered speech. The four divisions cover different scenarios of writing and reading. The Hanafi madhhab accepts testimony based on written iqrar under certain conditions.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment of a right or debt; can be audible or visible (written).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first division of written iqrar, what does al-Qadi al-Nasafi require for a writing without speech to be considered iqrar?
A) The writing must be read aloud by the writer.
B) The writing must be sealed and formal.
C) The witnesses must say 'bear witness'.
D) The writing must be a letter to an absentee.

Key Takeaway
Written iqrar is valid under Hanafi law if it is formal and witnessed; the view of al-Nasafi that a sealed writing suffices is accepted in practice.

Testimony on Sales, Leases, and Gifts: When Proof of Ownership Is Needed
Rulings on conditions for testifying to sales, leases, and gifts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for testimony on sale, lease, purchase, and gift, and identify when proof of ownership is required.

Core Idea
Testimony on a lease does not require proving the lessor's ownership because even a usurper's lease is valid.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the varying requirements for testimony on different contracts. The key distinction is whether the transaction itself implies ownership or not. We will explore when the witness must prove ownership and when it is not needed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and the ruling
List each contract (marriage, lease, waqf, sale, purchase, gift) and note the ruling on testimony requirements.
2
Compare the possession scenario for sale
For sale, distinguish whether the item is in the seller's possession or in a third party's possession. If in third party, must prove seller's ownership.
3
Understand the rationale for lease
The text states that even a usurper's lease is valid, so testimony to lease does not require proving ownership.
4
Apply the exception for testifying against the seller
If testifying against the seller himself, no ownership proof is needed.
5
Summarize the conclusion for purchase and sale
For purchase testimony, ownership or possession of seller is needed; for sale testimony, mention seller's ownership or possession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنكاح لا يكون إلا قولاً، وكذا لو ادعى التزوج فشهدا له بأنها زوجته تقبل كما في الخلاصة. والإجارة كالبيع وتنعقد بالقول وبالتعاطي والوقف قول ولا يشترط في الشهادة به بيان الواقف على الصحيح على ما ذكره في وقف البزازية وشرطه لقبولها في كتاب الشهادات . ثم اعلم أنه إذا شهد بالبيع فإن كان المبيع في يد غير البائع فلا بد أن يشهد بملك البائع بخلاف ما إذا كان في يده وأما الشهادة بالإجارة فلا يشترط أن يشهدوا بأن العين المؤجرة ملك المؤجر والفرق أن إجارة الغاصب المغصوب صحيحة بلا إذن المالك ويستحق الأجرة؛ كذا في دعوى البزازية، وكذا في الشهادة بالشراء والقبض، وكذا الهبة مع القبض لا يحتاجان إلى الشهادة بالملك للبائع والواهب ؛ كذا في الصغرى والحاصل أنهم إذا شهدوا بالشراء لمدعيه فلا بد من الشهادة بملك المدعي أو البائع أو يد البائع أو أن البائع سلمها للمشتري، وفي الشهادة بالبيع لا بد من ذكر ملك البائع أو يده. وهذا إذا شهدوا بالبيع على غير البائع، فلو شهدوا به عليه لم يشترط شيء منهما كما في منية المفتي. ويشترط في الشهادة بالإقرار رؤية المقر لما في شهادات البزازية. وذكر الخصاف : رجل في بيت وحده ودخل عليه رجل ورآه ثم خرج وجلس على الباب وليس للبيت مسلك غيره فسمع إقراره من الباب بلا رؤية وجهه حل له أن يشهد بما أقر . وفي العيون رجل خبأ قوماً لرجل ثم سأله عن شيء فأقروهم يسمعون كلامه ويرونه وهو لا يراهم جازت شهادتهم وإن لم يروه وسمعوا كلامه لا تحل لهم الشهادة ا هـ . وفي الجامع الصغير شرط رؤية وجه المرأة ورأيت الإمام خالي أمرها بكشف الوجه وأمرها بالخروج ويؤيده ما في العيون كذا في الخلاصة. وفي جامع الفصولين: حسرت عن وجهها وقالت أنا فلانة بنت فلان بن فلان وهبت لزوجي مهري فلا يحتاج الشهود إلى شهادة عدلين أنها فلانة بنت فلان ما دامت حية إذ يمكن الشاهد أن يشير إليها، فإن ماتت فيحنئذ يحتاج الشهود إلى شهادة عدلين بنسبها . وقال قبله : لو أخبر الشاهد عدلان أن هذه المقرة فلانة بنت فلان يكفي هذا للشهادة على الاسم والنسب عندهما وعليه الفتوى
And marriage is only by statement, and likewise if he claims marriage and two witnesses testify that she is his wife, it is accepted, as in al-Khulasah. And lease is like sale, and it is concluded by statement and by mutual dealing (ta'ati), and waqf (endowment) is a statement, and it is not required in testimony to it to mention the endower according to the correct opinion, as mentioned in Waqf al-Bazzaziyyah and its condition for acceptance in the book of testimonies. Then know that when they testify to a sale, if the sold item is in the possession of other than the seller, then they must testify to the seller's ownership, contrary to when it is in his possession. As for testimony to a lease, it is not required that they testify that the leased asset is the property of the lessor, and the difference is that the lease of a usurped thing (ghasb) is valid without the owner's permission and the lessor is entitled to rent; thus in Da'wa al-Bazzaziyyah. And likewise in testimony to purchase and possession, and likewise a gift with possession do not require testimony to the ownership of the seller or donor; thus in al-Sughra. The conclusion is that when they testify to purchase for the claimant, it is necessary to testify to the ownership of the claimant or the seller or the seller's possession or that the seller delivered it to the buyer. And in testimony to a sale, it is necessary to mention the seller's ownership or his possession. This is when they testify to a sale against other than the seller; if they testify to it against the seller, neither is required, as in Munyat al-Mufti. And it is required in testimony to iqrar (acknowledgment) to see the confessor, as in Shahadat al-Bazzaziyyah. And al-Khassaf mentioned: A man was alone in a house, and another man entered upon him and saw him, then he left and sat at the door, and there was no other entrance to the house, so he heard his iqrar from the door without seeing his face; it is permissible for him to testify to what he acknowledged. And in al-Uyun: A man hid some people for another man, then he asked him about something, and they acknowledged while they heard his speech and saw him, but he did not see them; their testimony is valid. But if they heard his speech but did not see him, it is not permissible for them to testify. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, it is required to see the woman's face. And I saw my maternal uncle ordering her to uncover her face and ordering her to go out. And supporting it is what is in al-Uyun, thus in al-Khulasah. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: She uncovered her face and said: I am so-and-so daughter of so-and-so son of so-and-so, and I have given my mahr to my husband. So the witnesses do not need the testimony of two just men that she is so-and-so daughter of so-and-so as long as she is alive, since the witness can point to her. If she dies, then the witnesses need the testimony of two just men of her lineage. And he said before: If two just men inform the witness that this woman is so-and-so daughter of so-and-so, this is sufficient for testimony to the name and lineage according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and the fatwa is upon it.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a set of ruling statements on testimony for various contracts. It begins with marriage: testimony that a woman is a man's wife is accepted without proof of ownership. Lease is like sale in that it can be concluded by statement or mutual dealing (ta'ati). Waqf does not require naming the endower. For sale testimony, if the item is in the buyer's possession, no need to prove seller's ownership; if in a third party's possession, must prove seller's ownership. For lease, no need to prove lessor's ownership because even a usurper's lease is valid. Similarly, testimony to purchase and possession, and gift with possession, do not require proving donor's ownership. However, testimony to purchase for the claimant requires proving ownership or possession of the seller or delivery. Testimony to sale requires mentioning seller's ownership or possession, unless against the seller himself. For iqrar, the witness must see the confessor. Al-Khassaf allows testimony if the witness heard from behind a door without seeing the face, provided no other entrance. Al-Uyun requires seeing the confesee. For women, seeing the face is required to confirm identity. After death, testimony to lineage requires two witnesses. The fatwa is according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad that information from two just men suffices for name and lineage during life, but after death, direct testimony is needed.

Key Terms
تعاطي (ta'ati): Mutual dealing without explicit verbal offer and acceptance; a mode of concluding contracts like lease.
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment; testimony to iqrar requires seeing the confessor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is testimony to a lease not required to prove the lessor's ownership?
A) Because lease is a temporary contract.
B) Because even a usurper's lease is valid.
C) Because ownership is irrelevant in leases.
D) Because the lessor is always the owner.

Key Takeaway
Testimony on a lease does not require proving the lessor's ownership because the lease of a non-owner is valid under Hanafi law.

Testimony on Acknowledgment: The Requirement of Seeing the Confessor
Rulings on conditions for testifying to acknowledgment (iqrar) and lineage identification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the requirement of seeing the confessor for testimony on iqrar, and identify exceptions when hearing alone may suffice.

Core Idea
For testimony on iqrar, the witness must see the confessor; but in certain cases, hearing the voice is enough.

This passage also addresses the conditions for testifying to an acknowledgment (iqrar). The general rule is that the witness must see the person making the iqrar. However, the text provides nuanced exceptions from al-Khassaf and al-Uyun, and discusses cases involving women and lineage after death.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule for iqrar testimony
The witness must see the confessor.
2
Evaluate the exception from al-Khassaf
If the witness saw the person initially, then heard his iqrar from behind a door with no other entrance, it is permissible.
3
Distinguish the al-Uyun case
If the witness hid people who saw and heard the confessor, but the confessor did not see them, testimony is valid; but if they only heard without seeing, it is not valid.
4
Apply the requirement for women
Seeing the woman's face is required to confirm identity.
5
Handle testimony after death
For lineage, after death, two just men must testify to the person's lineage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنكاح لا يكون إلا قولاً، وكذا لو ادعى التزوج فشهدا له بأنها زوجته تقبل كما في الخلاصة. والإجارة كالبيع وتنعقد بالقول وبالتعاطي والوقف قول ولا يشترط في الشهادة به بيان الواقف على الصحيح على ما ذكره في وقف البزازية وشرطه لقبولها في كتاب الشهادات . ثم اعلم أنه إذا شهد بالبيع فإن كان المبيع في يد غير البائع فلا بد أن يشهد بملك البائع بخلاف ما إذا كان في يده وأما الشهادة بالإجارة فلا يشترط أن يشهدوا بأن العين المؤجرة ملك المؤجر والفرق أن إجارة الغاصب المغصوب صحيحة بلا إذن المالك ويستحق الأجرة؛ كذا في دعوى البزازية، وكذا في الشهادة بالشراء والقبض، وكذا الهبة مع القبض لا يحتاجان إلى الشهادة بالملك للبائع والواهب ؛ كذا في الصغرى والحاصل أنهم إذا شهدوا بالشراء لمدعيه فلا بد من الشهادة بملك المدعي أو البائع أو يد البائع أو أن البائع سلمها للمشتري، وفي الشهادة بالبيع لا بد من ذكر ملك البائع أو يده. وهذا إذا شهدوا بالبيع على غير البائع، فلو شهدوا به عليه لم يشترط شيء منهما كما في منية المفتي. ويشترط في الشهادة بالإقرار رؤية المقر لما في شهادات البزازية. وذكر الخصاف : رجل في بيت وحده ودخل عليه رجل ورآه ثم خرج وجلس على الباب وليس للبيت مسلك غيره فسمع إقراره من الباب بلا رؤية وجهه حل له أن يشهد بما أقر . وفي العيون رجل خبأ قوماً لرجل ثم سأله عن شيء فأقروهم يسمعون كلامه ويرونه وهو لا يراهم جازت شهادتهم وإن لم يروه وسمعوا كلامه لا تحل لهم الشهادة ا هـ . وفي الجامع الصغير شرط رؤية وجه المرأة ورأيت الإمام خالي أمرها بكشف الوجه وأمرها بالخروج ويؤيده ما في العيون كذا في الخلاصة. وفي جامع الفصولين: حسرت عن وجهها وقالت أنا فلانة بنت فلان بن فلان وهبت لزوجي مهري فلا يحتاج الشهود إلى شهادة عدلين أنها فلانة بنت فلان ما دامت حية إذ يمكن الشاهد أن يشير إليها، فإن ماتت فيحنئذ يحتاج الشهود إلى شهادة عدلين بنسبها . وقال قبله : لو أخبر الشاهد عدلان أن هذه المقرة فلانة بنت فلان يكفي هذا للشهادة على الاسم والنسب عندهما وعليه الفتوى
