Testimony by Hearsay for Lineage and Irrevocability of Judgment
Discusses hearsay testimony for lineage and the partial overturning of judgments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for accepting hearsay testimony on lineage in Hanafi fiqh and apply the rule that a judgment on lineage is overturned only for inheritance, not lineage itself.

Core Idea
A judgment on lineage is irrevocable for the public, but may be overturned for inheritance when a closer heir appears.

In Hanafi law, lineage (nasab) is established by testimony, including hearsay (tashammu') under specific conditions. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that while judgments on lineage are generally irrevocable, an exception exists: when a closer heir emerges, the judgment is overturned for inheritance purposes but the lineage relationship remains intact. Understanding this distinction is crucial for proper application in inheritance cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
First, note that the passage states judgments on lineage are irrevocable because they affect the public, similar to marriage, freedom, and clientage.
This establishes the baseline: lineage is a matter of public record.
2
Locate the exception
Find the exception from al-Muhit: if a closer heir appears, the judgment is overturned for inheritance but not for lineage itself.
The key is distinguishing between the financial effect (inheritance) and the personal status (lineage).
3
Understand the conditions for hearsay testimony
The passage then lists conditions: the witness must have heard from two trustworthy persons (adl), the informants must not be the parties, and the witness must not have been summoned to testify.
These conditions ensure reliability of indirect testimony.
4
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Work through the example: a stranger's lineage cannot be testified to until two trustworthy men from his town inform the witness.
Geographical proximity adds reliability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن القضاء بالنسب مما لا يقبل النقض لكونه على الكافة كالنكاح والحرية والولاء كما في الصغرى وكذا كتبنا في الفوائد أن القضاء على الكافة في الأربعة لكن يستثنى من النسب ما في المحيط من باب الشهادة بالتسامع : شهدا أن فلان بن فلان مات وهذا ابن أخيه ووارثه قضى بالنسب والإرث، ثم أقام آخر البينة أنه ابن الميت ووارثه ينقض الأوّل ويقضى للثاني لأن الابن مقدم على ابن الأخ، ولا تنافي بين الأوّل والثاني لجواز أن يكون له ابن وابن أخ فينقض القضاء في حق الميراث لا في حق النسب حتى يبقى الأول ابن عم له حتى يرث منه إذا مات ولم يترك وارثاً آخر أقرب منه، فإنه أقام آخر البينة أن الميت الأوّل فلان بن فلان ونسبه إلى أب أخر غير الأب الذي نسبه إلى الأوّل فإنه ينظر؛ إن ادعى ابن أخيه لا ينقض القضاء الأوّل لأنه لما أثبت نفسه من الأوّل خرج عن هذه أن الثلاثة، فلو كان المخبر في الثلاثة عدلاً أيضاً حل لهم أن يشهدوا ثم في الثلاثة إذا ثبت الشهرة عندهما بخبر عدلين يجب الإخبار بلفظ الشهادة وفي الموت لما ثبت بخبر الواحد بالإجماع لا يجب بل يكتفى بمجرد الإخبار . قوله : (فينقض القضاء في حق الميراث لا في حق النسب هذا مناف لقوله «لكن يستثنى من النسب الخ . من يثق به ومن في يده شيء سوى الرقيق لك أن تشهد أنه له وإن فسر للقاضي أنه يكون محلاً لإثباته في إنسان آخر وليس في البينة الثانية زيادة إثبات إلى آخر ما ذكره. والمراد بقوله «من يثق به» غير الخصم إذ لو أخبره رجل أنه فلان بن فلان لا يسعه أن يعتمد على خبره ويشهد بنفسه لأنه لو جاز له ذلك الجاز للقاضي القضاء بقوله ؛ كذا في خزانة المفتين . وشرط فيها للقبول في النسب أن يخبره عدلان من غير استشهاد الرجل فإن أقام الرجل شاهدين عنده على نسبه لا يسعه أن يشهد، وإذا كان الرجل غريباً لا يسعه أن يشهد بنسبه حتى يلقى من أهل بلده رجلين عدلين فيشهد أن عنده على نسبه. قال الجصاص : وهو الصحيح ا اهـ.
Then know that judgment about lineage is not subject to annulment because it concerns the public like marriage, freedom, and clientage (wala) as in al-Sughra. Similarly, we have written in al-Fawa'id that judgment concerning the public in the four [matters] but an exception from lineage is what is in al-Muhit from the chapter of testimony by hearsay: two witnesses testified that so-and-so son of so-and-so died, and this is his brother's son and his heir; judgment was given regarding lineage and inheritance. Then another person established evidence that he is the son of the deceased and his heir; the first judgment is overturned and judgment is given for the second because the son is preferred over the brother's son. There is no contradiction between the first and second because it is possible that he had a son and a brother's son, so the judgment is overturned regarding inheritance but not regarding lineage, so that the first remains as a paternal cousin such that he inherits from him if he dies without leaving any closer heir. Then if another establishes evidence that the first deceased is so-and-so son of so-and-so and traces his lineage to another father other than the father to whom the first traced him, then it is examined: if the brother's son claims, the first judgment is not overturned because when he established himself from the first, he came out from this... [text unclear] ...the three, if the informant in the three is also trustworthy, it is permissible for them to testify. Then in the three, when notoriety is established to them by the news of two trustworthy persons, informing with the wording of testimony is obligatory; and in death, since it is established by the news of one by consensus, it is not obligatory, rather mere informing suffices. His statement: 'So the judgment is overturned regarding inheritance but not regarding lineage' contradicts his statement 'but an exception from lineage' etc. 'From one whom he trusts' and 'from one in whose hand is something besides slaves, you may testify that it is his' and even if he explains to the judge that it is a place for establishing it in another person, and in the second evidence there is no additional establishment, etc. The meaning of his statement 'from one whom he trusts' is other than the opponent. For if a man informs him that he is so-and-so son of so-and-so, he cannot rely on his news and testify himself, because if that were permissible for him, it would be permissible for the judge to rule by his statement. This is in Khizanat al-Muftiyyin. He conditioned therein for acceptance in lineage that two trustworthy persons inform him without the man having them summoned as witnesses. If the man produces two witnesses before him regarding his lineage, he cannot testify. And if the man is a stranger, he cannot testify to his lineage until he meets two trustworthy men from his town, then he testifies that he has knowledge of his lineage. Al-Jassas said: and this is correct.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage addresses shahada bil tashammu' for lineage (nasab) and the possibility of overturning a judgment based on it. The general rule is that judgments on lineage are irrevocable because they affect the public (like marriage, freedom, and wala). However, there is an exception: if a judgment on lineage is made based on hearsay and then a closer heir appears with evidence, the judgment can be overturned regarding inheritance but not regarding lineage itself. For example, if a court declares a nephew as heir, and then a son appears, the son takes the inheritance, but the nephew remains a cousin. The passage also discusses conditions for accepting hearsay testimony in lineage: the informant must be trustworthy and not a party, and the witness must have received the information from two trustworthy persons without being asked to testify. If a man produces witnesses to his lineage, that does not entitle another to testify. For a stranger, one must meet two trustworthy men from his town. Al-Jassas confirms this as correct.

Key Terms
النسب (al-nasab): Lineage or familial relationship; the subject of testimony by hearsay.
التسامع (al-tashammu'): Hearsay; indirect testimony where the witness did not directly observe but heard from others.
نقض القضاء (naqd al-qada): Overturning a legal judgment; in this context, partial overturning for inheritance only.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example from al-Muhit, if a court declares a nephew as heir based on hearsay, and then a son appears, what happens to the judgment?
A) The entire judgment is overturned, including lineage.
B) The judgment is overturned for inheritance but lineage remains.
C) The judgment stands; the son cannot inherit.
D) The case is re-decided from scratch.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, testimony by hearsay on lineage is accepted with conditions, and a judgment on lineage is partly irrevocable: it can be overturned for inheritance but not for the lineage relation itself.

Testifying to Ownership Based on Possession (Yad) in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling with proof and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi rule for testifying to ownership based on possession and identify the exceptions for unlikely possessors and pre-owned items.

Core Idea
Possession suffices for testimony unless the possessor is unlikely to own such an item.

In Hanafi law, possession (yad) is a strong indicator of ownership and generally suffices for testifying. However, jurists carved out exceptions when the possession is improbable or the item was previously seen in another's hands. This lesson unpacks the general rule, the proof, the intra-Hanafi dispute on required conviction, and the key exceptions.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Identify the rule: if you see something in someone's hand, you may testify it is his, because possession is the primary indicator of ownership.
The text begins: 'ومن في يده شيء سوى الرقيق لك أن تشهد أنه له'
2
Understand the proof (dalil)
Possession is the ultimate reference in all causes (أقصى ما يستدل به على الملك) – it is relied upon due to custom and necessity.
The proof is based on istihsan and 'urf, not a specific text.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf requires internal conviction that it is his, while Muhammad's absolute statement from the narration suffices with possession alone. The preferred view (al-Sadr al-Shahid, followed in Fath al-Qadir) is that possession suffices.
This is a dispute within the school on the degree of certainty required.
4
Apply the exceptions
Exception 1: If the possessor is unlikely to own such an item (e.g., a sweeper with a pearl, an ignorant person with a book), mere possession does not justify testimony. Exception 2: If one has seen the item in another's hand before, testimony is not allowed unless a transfer is confirmed.
These exceptions prevent false testimony based on improbable possession.
5
Consider special cases
Slaves are excepted because they have their own hand; a slave woman claiming freedom cannot be married based on possession. If the owner is a woman who stays at home but the property is famous, testimony may be based on fame (istihsan), but this is critiqued as testimony by hearsay.
The author also notes two scenarios where testimony is not allowed: (a) only hearsay, (b) seeing the owner but not the property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن في يده شيء سوى الرقيق لك أن تشهد أنه له لأن اليد أقصى ما يستدل الدلالة به على الملك إذ هي مرجع في الأسباب كلها فيكتفى بها. وعن أبي يوسف أنه يشترط ذلك أن يقع في قلبه أنه له قالوا ويحتمل أن يكون هذا تفسيراً لإطلاق محمد في الرواية. قال في فتح القدير قال الصدر الشهيد و به نأخذ فهو قولهم جميعاً ! اهـ. فلو رأى درة في يد كناس أو كتاباً في يد جاهل لا يشهد بالملك له بمجرد يده؛ كذا في البزازية. ومن مشايخنا قال إنها دليل الملك التصرف لكونها متنوعة إلى أمانة وملك قلنا: والتصرف يتنوع أيضاً إلى أصالة ونيابة وظاهر كلام المؤلف أنه عاين المالك والملك فإذا رآه في يد آخر فجاء الأوّل وادعى الملك وسعه أن يشهد أنه له بناء على يده قالوا : وكذا إذا عاين المالك بحدوده دون الملك استحساناً لأن النسب يثبت بالتسامع . له وفرع على هذا الناصحي بأن المالك لو كان امرأة لا تخرج ولا يراها الرجال فإن كان الملك مشهوراً أنه لها جاز أن يشهد عليه لأن شهرة الاسم كالمعاينة ا هـ . وأورد عليه لزوم الشهادة بالمال بالتسامع، وأجيب بأنه في ضمن الشهادة بالنسب كما في النهاية وتعقبه في فتح القدير بأن مجرد ثبوت نسبه بالشهادة عند القاضي لم يوجب ثبوت ملكه لتلك الضيعة لولا الشهادة، به وكذا المقصود ليس إثبات النسب بل الملك في الضيعة ا هـ . أن مسألتان : إحداهما أن لا يعاينهما وإنما سمع وخرج لفلان كذا. الثانية أن يعاين المالك لا الملك فلا يحل له أن يشهد لكونه مجازفاً في الأولى وفي الثانية لم يحصل له العلم بالمحدود. وأشار المؤلف رحمه الله إلى أن من رأى شيئاً في يد إنسان ولم يره قبل ذلك في يد غيره فإن له أن يشتريه منه فإن كان رآه قبله في يد غيره فإن أخبره بانتقال الملك إليه أو بالوكالة منه حل الشراء وإلا فلا. وكذا لو رأى جارية في يد إنسان ثم رآها في بلد أخرى وقالت أنا حرة الأصل لا يحل له أن ينكحها وسيأتي تمامه في الكراهية . واستثنى المصنف الرقيق أي العبد والأمة وهو مقيد بما إذا كانا كبيرين لأن لهما يداً على قوله : (لا يحل له أن ينكحها لعله مبني على الرواية الآتية قريباً عن أبي حنيفة تأمل قوله : (أن
His statement: 'And from one in whose hand is something besides slaves, you may testify that it is his' because possession is the furthest thing that indicates ownership, as it is the reference in all causes, so it suffices. And from Abu Yusuf that he stipulates that it should occur in his heart that it is his. They said: and it is possible that this is an interpretation of Muhammad's absolute [statement] in the narration. He said in Fath al-Qadir: al-Sadr al-Shahid said and we take by it, so it is the saying of all of them! So if he sees a pearl in the hand of a sweeper or a book in the hand of an ignorant person, he does not testify that it is his by mere possession; such is in al-Bazzaziyya. And some of our teachers said that it is a proof of ownership due to possession, because it varies into trust and ownership; we said: and possession also varies into principal and agency. And the apparent meaning of the author's statement is that he witnessed the owner and the owned; so if he sees it in another's hand, and the first comes and claims ownership, he may testify that it is his based on possession. They said: similarly, if he witnesses the owner by his boundaries without the owned, it is permissible by istihsan because lineage is established by hearsay. And al-Nasihi branched on this: if the owner is a woman who does not go out and men cannot see her, and if the property is well-known to be hers, it is permissible to testify about it because the fame of the name is like witnessing. It was objected that this necessitates testimony about property by hearsay, and it was answered that it is within the testimony about lineage as in al-Nihaya. But Fath al-Qadir criticized that mere establishment of his lineage by testimony before the judge does not necessitate the establishment of his ownership of that estate without the testimony, and similarly the purpose is not to establish lineage but ownership of the estate. There are two issues: one is that he does not witness them but only hears and it is said it belongs to so-and-so; the second is that he witnesses the owner but not the owned, so it is not permissible for him to testify because he would be speaking without knowledge in the first, and in the second he does not have knowledge of the bounded thing. And the author indicated that if a person sees something in the hand of another and did not see it before in the hand of someone else, then he may buy it from him. And if he had seen it before in the hand of someone else, then if he tells him of transfer of ownership or agency from him, purchase is permissible; otherwise no. Similarly, if he sees a slave girl in the hand of a man and then sees her in another country saying 'I am free by origin', it is not permissible for him to marry her; and its completion will come in the chapter of karahiyya. The author excepted slaves, i.e., male and female slave, and it is restricted to when they are adult because they have possession based on his statement: 'It is not permissible for him to marry her' perhaps it is based on the narration that will come soon from Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage discusses testifying to ownership based on possession (yad). The general rule is that if one sees an item in someone's hand, he may testify that it is his because possession is a strong indicator of ownership. However, there are exceptions: (1) if the possessor is a lowly person like a sweeper with a pearl, or an ignorant person with a book, mere possession is not sufficient due to unlikelihood of ownership. (2) If one has previously seen the item in another's hand, he cannot testify based on current possession unless he is informed of a valid transfer. (3) Slaves are excepted because they have their own hand (they can possess). A slave woman claiming freedom cannot be married based on possession. The text also mentions a dispute about whether internal conviction is required (Abu Yusuf's view) or mere possession suffices (Muhammad's view); the preferred view is that possession suffices unless there is reason to doubt. A branch from al-Nasihi: if the owner is a woman who stays at home and her property is famous, one can testify based on fame. This is criticized as testimony by hearsay, but defended as within lineage. The author concludes by distinguishing two scenarios: (a) when one only hears but does not witness, and (b) when one sees the owner but not the property; in both cases, testimony is not allowed.

Key Terms
اليد (al-yad): Possession or physical control over an item; used as a basis for testifying to ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if you see a pearl in the hand of a sweeper, can you testify that it is his?
A) Yes, because possession is sufficient.
B) No, because a sweeper is unlikely to own a pearl.
C) Yes, but only if he confirms ownership.
D) No, because only slaves can be testified about by possession.

Key Takeaway
Possession suffices for testimony unless the possessor is unlikely to own such an item or the item was previously seen in another's hand.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Testifying to Ownership Based on Possession
Ruling on testifying that an item in someone's hand belongs to them

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for testifying to ownership based on possession, identify the exceptions (adult slaves, contradictory reports, and lack of knowledge), and apply the rule to practical scenarios.

Core Idea
Possession is the strongest indicator of ownership, but testimony requires no contrary knowledge and excludes adult slaves.

In Hanafi law, possession (yad) is taken as prima facie evidence of ownership. A witness who sees an item in someone's hand may generally testify that it belongs to that person. However, this rule has important exceptions and conditions, especially when the possessor is an adult slave or when the witness has hearsay knowledge. This lesson examines the ruling, its proof, the intra-Hanafi difference with Abu Yusuf, and the practical limits derived from the text of al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq.

Guided Path
1
State the General Ruling
Identify the act (testifying to ownership) and its ruling (permissible, jāʾiz) based on the text: 'Whoever has in his hand something other than a slave, you may testify that it is his.'
The exception for slaves is explicitly mentioned.
2
Identify the Proof (Dalīl)
The text gives the reasoning: 'because the hand is the utmost that indicates ownership, as it is the basis for all causes.' This is an aqlī (rational) proof based on the evidentiary value of possession.
No specific Quran or hadith is cited; it is a principle of testimony.
3
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilāf
Abu Yusuf requires inner certainty (yaqīn) that the item belongs to the possessor, while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad suffice with possession unless contradicted. The relied-upon (muftā bihī) view is the majority position.
The difference affects cases where possession alone may be ambiguous (e.g., a book in the hand of an ignorant person).
4
Apply the Exceptions
The ruling does not apply to adult slaves (who have their own 'hand'), or when two upright witnesses contradict possession, or when the witness only has hearsay about ownership.
Minors or those who cannot express themselves are treated as goods; possession suffices for the possessor.

يكون هذا تفسيراً لإطلاق محمد في الرواية. قال في فتح القدير قال الصدر الشهيد و به نأخذ فهو قولهم جميعاً ! اهـ. فلو رأى درة في يد كناس أو كتاباً في يد جاهل لا يشهد بالملك له بمجرد يده؛ كذا في البزازية. ومن مشايخنا قال إنها دليل الملك التصرف لكونها متنوعة إلى أمانة وملك قلنا: والتصرف يتنوع أيضاً إلى أصالة ونيابة وظاهر كلام المؤلف أنه عاين المالك والملك فإذا رآه في يد آخر فجاء الأوّل وادعى الملك وسعه وعلى هذا فالمراد بالكبير في كلامهم هنا من يعبر عن نفسه، سواء كان بالغاً أو لا كما في النهاية . ثم اعلم أنه إنما يشهد بالملك لذي اليد بشرط أن لا يخبره عدلان بأنه لغيره فلو أخبراه لم تجز له الشهادة منه من غيره أن يدعيه الأوّل، فما في الفتاوى فيما إذا ادعاه المالك وما في الشرح فيما إذا لم يدعه .
His statement: (And whoever has in his hand something other than a slave, you may testify that it is his) because the hand is the utmost that indicates ownership, as it is the basis for all causes, so it suffices. And from Abu Yusuf that he conditions that it enters his heart that it is his. They said: it is likely that this is an interpretation of Muhammad's absolute statement in the narration. It is stated in Fath al-Qadir: al-Sadr al-Shahid said: we adopt this, so it is all of their statement. So if he sees a pearl in the hand of a cleaner, or a book in the hand of an ignorant person, he does not testify to ownership for him merely by his hand; as in al-Bazzaziyya. And some of our scholars said that it is evidence of ownership by disposition, because it varies between trust and ownership. We said: and disposition also varies between original and deputyship. And the apparent meaning of the author's statement is that he actually saw the owner and the property; so if he sees it in another's hand and then the first comes and claims ownership, it is permissible for him to testify that it is his based on his hand. They said: and likewise if he sees the owner with its boundaries but not the property, by istihsan, because lineage is established by hearsay. And al-Nasihi derived from this that if the owner is a woman who does not go out and men cannot see her, and the property is well-known to be hers, it is permissible to testify to it because fame of the name is like visual confirmation. An objection was raised about the necessity of testifying to property by hearsay, and it was answered that it is within the testimony of lineage, as in al-Nihaya. And it was refuted in Fath al-Qadir that mere establishment of lineage by testimony before the judge does not necessitate establishment of ownership of that property without testimony. And likewise the purpose is not to establish lineage but ownership of the property. So there are two issues: first, that he does not see them but only hears so-and-so has such-and-such. Second, that he sees the owner but not the property, so it is not lawful for him to testify because in the first it is reckless, and in the second he did not acquire knowledge of the bounded thing. And the author indicated that whoever sees something in the hand of a person and did not see it before in another's hand, he may buy it from him. But if he saw it before in another's hand, then if he informs him of transfer of ownership or agency from him, purchase is lawful; otherwise not. And likewise if he sees a slave-girl in the hand of a person then sees her in another country and she says 'I am originally free', it is not lawful for him to marry her, and its completion will come in the chapter on dislikes. And the author excepted slaves, i.e., male and female slaves, and it is restricted to when they are adult because they have a hand over themselves. Regarding his statement: (it is not lawful for him to marry her) perhaps it is based on the narration forthcoming from Abu Hanifa. Contemplate his statement: (that her own self repels the hand of another from her, so evidence of ownership is absent. And from Abu Hanifa that it is lawful for him to testify in them also, by analogy to clothes, and the difference is what we explained. And if they are minors who cannot express themselves, like goods, they have no hand, so he may testify to ownership for the possessor. And on this, the meaning of 'adult' in their speech here is one who can express himself, whether he is mature or not, as in al-Nihaya. Then know that he only testifies to ownership for the possessor on condition that two upright persons do not inform him that it is for another; if they so inform, it is not permissible for him to testify to ownership for him, as in al-Khulasa and we have mentioned it. And the author indicated that if the judge sees an item in the hand of a person, it is permissible for him to judge ownership for him, as in al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyya. And from this it appears that the statement of the commentator in explaining that if the witness interprets to the judge that he testifies from hearing or from seeing the hand, it is not accepted, and that the judge may not judge based on his own hearing even if it is widely transmitted nor based on his own sight of something in a person's hand, is a mistake, unless one interprets it as what they said: if he sees something in the hand of a person then sees it in the hand of another, he does not take it from him if another claims it first. So what is in al-Fatawa is when the owner claims it, and what is in the commentary is when he does not claim it.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a ruling explanation from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqā'iq. The author, Ibn Nujaym, explains the Hanafi position on when a witness may testify to ownership based on possession (yad). The general principle is that possession is prima facie evidence of ownership, so a witness who sees an item in someone's hand may testify that it belongs to that person, provided the witness has no contrary knowledge. However, there are exceptions: if the possessor is a slave (adult) who has his own hand, or if the item is commonly known to belong to another. For adult slaves, their self-awareness allows them to assert ownership, so possession is not decisive. For minors or those who cannot express themselves, possession is stronger. The passage also distinguishes between directly seeing both owner and property versus only hearing about ownership. In the latter case, testimony is not allowed. The text records a difference between Abu Yusuf and the general position: Abu Yusuf requires an inner conviction, but the relied-upon view is that mere possession suffices unless contradicted by two upright witnesses. The passage concludes by discussing the judge's own knowledge: if the judge sees an item in a person's hand, he may rule based on that, contrary to some statements that would forbid it. The author reconciles the apparent contradiction by noting different scenarios.

Key Terms
اليد (al-yad): Possession; physical control of an object, used as evidence of ownership in testimony.
التسامع (al-tasāmuʿ): Hearsay; knowledge obtained through widespread reputation or common report.
المعاينة (al-muʿāyana): Direct visual observation; certain knowledge by seeing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq, when is a witness NOT allowed to testify to ownership based on possession?
A) When the possessor is a minor who cannot express himself.
B) When the possessor is an adult slave.
C) When the witness sees a pearl in the hand of a cleaner.
D) When the item was previously seen in the hand of another person.

Key Takeaway
Possession is strong but not conclusive evidence of ownership; testimony based on it has conditions, especially regarding slaves and contradictory reports.

Hearsay Testimony and the Judge's Personal Knowledge
Ruling on acceptance of hearsay testimony and judge's knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hearsay testimony, identify the exceptions, and explain the dispute regarding the judge's reliance on his own knowledge.

Core Idea
Hearsay testimony is rejected except for death and waqf; the judge cannot rule by his own knowledge.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq addresses two interrelated issues: the validity of testimony based on hearsay, and whether a judge may use his personal knowledge when issuing a verdict. The Hanafi school generally requires direct knowledge for testimony, but makes pragmatic exceptions for matters of public knowledge. The ruling on the judge's knowledge reflects a shift in the late school toward strict procedural objectivity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
State that testimony interpreted as based on hearsay (tasāmuʿ) or mere possession (muʿāyanat al-yad) is not accepted. This is the correct view (ṣaḥīḥ) as noted by Miskīn.
Note that the witness must interpret (fassara) – the judgment depends on what the witness says, not on the form of the testimony.
2
Identify the exceptions
Recognize the exceptions: death (al-mawt) and, according to al-ʿImādī, waqf. Some scholars also include other matters of common knowledge.
The word 'al-mawqif' in the text is likely a misreading of 'al-mawqūf' (waqf).
3
Analyze the Quranic evidence
Examine the two verses cited: 'except those who testify to the truth and they know' (43:86) and 'we testified only to what we knew' (12:81). These prove that knowledge (ʿilm) is a condition for valid testimony.
The verses are qaṭʿī al-thubūt, so they provide strong evidence.
4
Examine the dispute on judge's knowledge
Contrast the view of al-Zaylaʿī (judge cannot give a binding judgment based on his own knowledge) with the opposite view. Note that the fatwa follows the later scholars who forbid it.
The judge may still leave the property in the possessor's hand pending proof – this is not a final verdict.
5
Understand the practical significance
The intra-Hanafi differences yield practical consequences: for example, a witness may say 'I testify because I heard from the people' – such testimony is rejected except for death and waqf. The judge's knowledge cannot be used to overturn procedural requirements.
This protects the rights of litigants who do not have the opportunity to cross-examine the judge's private knowledge.

Source Text

قوله : (وإن فسر للقاضي أنه يشهد له بالتسامع أو بمعاينة اليد لا تقبل) وهذا هو الصحيح كما ذكره مسكين في شرحه لكنه استثنى الموت والموقف فتقبل، ولو فسر للقاضي أنه أخبره من يثق به واستثنى العمادي في الفصول الوقف فلو شهدا به وقالا نشهد بالتسامع ما القاضي الخ) مقول القول قوله : (سهو إلا أن يحمل الخ) رده العلامة المقدسي بأنه لا سهو في كلام الزيلعي، ومراده أن القاضي لا يقضي قضاء محكماً مبرماً بحيث لو ادعى الخصم لا يقبل منه بدليل صرح به قبيل هذا في أول القولة بأنه يقضي به قضاء ترك بمعنى أنه يترك في يد ذي اليد ما دام خصمه لا حجة له؛ حموي وأقول لا حاجة إلى تكلف إبداء وجه التوفيق ودفع المعارضة لأن المسألة مختلف فيها، فما في الزيلعي يبتنى على قول المتأخرين من أن القاضي ليس له أن يقضي بعلمه وهو المفتى به، وما في الخلاصة والبزازية يبتنى على مقابلة أبو السعود وفي الحواشي السعدية : المخالفة ولا يتوهم بين ما ذكر الزيلعي وما في النهاية فإن ما في شرح الكنز هو ما إذا رأى القاضي قبل حال القضاء ثم رأى حال قضائه في يد غيره كما لا يخفى .اهـ. قول المصنف : (وإن فسر للقاضي الخ) بقي في كلام المصنف مسألة . من المتن لم يذكرها المؤلف وهي قوله بعد هذه المسألة : ومن شهد أنه حضر دفن فلان أو صلى على جنازته فهو معاينة حتى لو فسر للقاضي قبل قال الشارح الزيلعي : لأنه لم يشهد إلا بما علم فوجب قبولها لدخوله تحت قوله تعالى إلا من شهد بالحق وهم يعلمون [الزخرف: ٨٦] وقال تعالى وما شهدنا إلا بما علمنا ﴾ [يوسف: ۸۱] قوله : (واستثنى العمادي في الفصول الوقف الخ) أفتى العلامة ملاعلي التركماني بعدم القبول مستنداً إلى إطلاق عبارة الكنز والزيلعي والعيني والوقاية والنقاية والمختار والاختيار ثم قال : وفي الخيرية من الشهادة والشهادة على الوقف بالسماع أن يقول الشاهد أشهد به لأني سمعت من الناس أو بسبب أني سمعت من الناس
His statement: (And if he interprets to the judge that he testifies for him by hearsay or by seeing the hand, it is not accepted) and this is the correct view as mentioned by Miskīn in his commentary, but he excepted death and the [waqf] so it is accepted. And if he interprets to the judge that a trustworthy person informed him, and al-ʿImādī in al-Fuṣūl excepted waqf, so if two testify to it and say 'we testify by hearsay' ... the judge ...) The spoken part of his statement: (a mistake unless interpreted...) al-Maqdisī refuted it, saying there is no mistake in al-Zaylaʿī's words, and his meaning is that the judge does not give a binding definitive judgment such that if the opponent claims it is not accepted, as evidenced by his earlier statement that he gives a judgment of leaving, meaning he leaves it in the hand of the possessor as long as the opponent has no proof; Ḥamawī said: there is no need to contrive a reconciliation because the issue is disputed. What is in al-Zaylaʿī is based on the later scholars' view that the judge may not judge by his own knowledge, and that is the fatwa. What is in al-Khulāṣa and al-Bazzāziyya is based on the opposing view of Abū al-Suʿūd. And in al-Ḥawāshī al-Saʿdiyya: there is no contradiction between what al-Zaylaʿī mentioned and what is in al-Nihāya, because what is in Sharḥ al-Kanz applies when the judge saw before the state of judgment and then saw it during judgment in another's hand, as is not hidden. So the author's statement: (And if he interprets to the judge...) there remains in the author's text an issue not mentioned by him, which is his statement after this issue: And whoever testifies that he attended the burial of so-and-so or prayed over his funeral, that is visual observation, even if he interprets to the judge beforehand. Al-Zaylaʿī said: because he only testified to what he knew, so it must be accepted, as it falls under the verse of Allah 'except those who testify to the truth and they know' [43:86] and He said 'and we testified only to what we knew' [12:81]. His statement: (and al-ʿImādī in al-Fuṣūl excepted waqf...) Muftī ʿAlī al-Turkumānī gave a fatwa of non-acceptance based on the absolute wording of al-Kanz, al-Zaylaʿī, al-ʿAynī, al-Wiqāya, al-Niqāya, al-Mukhtār, and al-Ikhtiyār. Then he said: and in al-Khayriyya regarding testimony and testimony on waqf by hearing, the witness should say: I testify because I heard from the people or because I heard from the people
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage discusses the acceptance of testimony when the witness interprets to the judge that his testimony is based on hearsay (tasāmuʿ) or on seeing the hand (muʿāyanat al-yad). The ruling is that such testimony is not accepted, except in cases of death and (according to some) waqf. The text then addresses a dispute about whether a judge can rule based on his own knowledge. The commentator al-Zaylaʿī held that the judge cannot give a binding judgment based on his own knowledge, while others allowed it. The author reconciles this by noting that the judge may leave the property in the possessor's hand until a claimant proves otherwise. The passage also cites Quranic evidence that testimony must be based on knowledge. Finally, there is a reference to an exception for waqf: some scholars accept hearsay testimony for waqf because it is a public matter, while others reject it.

Key Terms
التسامع (al-tasāmuʿ): Hearsay; knowledge from widespread report or common reputation, not direct observation.
الموقف (al-mawqif): Possibly a typo for 'الموقوف' (endowment/waqf). The context discusses acceptance of hearsay for waqf.
علم القاضي (ʿilm al-qāḍī): The judge's personal knowledge of a case, separate from evidence presented in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main reason hearsay testimony (tasāmuʿ) is generally not accepted in Hanafi fiqh?
A) The Quran commands that testimony must be from two witnesses.
B) It lacks the certainty (yaqīn) required for testimony, as indicated by Quranic verses requiring knowledge.
C) The judge's personal knowledge is always sufficient, so hearsay is unnecessary.
D) Hearsay is only accepted in criminal cases.

Key Takeaway
Hearsay testimony is rejected unless it concerns death or (according to some) waqf; the judge cannot use his personal knowledge for a binding verdict.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Testimony by Hearsay or Seeing Possession: Ruling, Proof, and Dispute
Explains ruling on testimony by hearsay or seeing possession with proof, conditions, and dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony based on hearsay or seeing possession, identify the Quranic proof, explain the exceptions, and distinguish the mufta bihi position from the opposing view.

Core Idea
Testimony requires direct knowledge; hearsay and mere possession are insufficient, except in death and endowment.

This lesson unpacks a key evidentiary rule: when a witness testifies based on hearsay (tasāmu') or merely seeing possession (muʿāyanat al-yad), the testimony is generally rejected. We will examine the Quranic foundation, the conditions for acceptance, and an important intra-Hanafi dispute about what happens when the witness explains the hearsay basis to the judge. The author of al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq settles the dispute in favour of the majority view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and its rationale
The passage opens stating that testimony by hearsay or seeing possession is not accepted. The reason is that possession alone does not prove ownership; it could be due to lease or loan.
Even if the witness explains the basis, the ruling depends on further analysis.
2
Locate the dalīl and understand the wajh al-dalālah
The proof is from the Qur’ān: verses requiring testimony to be based on knowledge (al-Zukhruf 43:86, Yūsuf 12:81). These imply that hearsay does not constitute knowledge.
The authorities also note an exception by istiḥsān for certain matters.
3
Note the conditions and exceptions
The witness may testify for a possessor only if no two just men contradict. Exceptions include death and endowment (waqf), where hearsay testimony is sometimes accepted because these matters are known by widespread reporting.
The judge's own observation is also discussed: he may judge ownership based on direct sight, but not on hearsay.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafī dispute
The main dispute: if a witness explains to the judge that his testimony is based on hearsay, is it accepted? Some (al-Imādī, al-Khulāṣa) say yes for death and endowment; the majority (Qāḍīkhān, most mutūn) say no because hearsay indicates lack of certainty.
The author sides with the majority, citing that the texts and Qāḍīkhān's corrections are more reliable.
5
Determine the muftā bihī position
The relied-upon position: testimony by hearsay is not accepted even if the witness explains, except in the specific matters of death and endowment where it is accepted without explanation. If the witness says 'I heard', it is rejected.
This is based on the authority of Qāḍīkhān and the majority of the mutūn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يشهد له بالتسامع أو بمعاينة اليد لا تقبل. أنفسهما تدفع يد الغير عنهما فانعدم دليل الملك، وعن أبي حنيفة أنه يحل له أن يشهد فيهما أيضاً اعتباراً بالثياب والفرق ما بيناه وإن كانا صغيرين لا يعبران عن أنفسهما كالمتاع لا يد لهما فله أن يشهد بالملك لذوي اليد، وعلى هذا فالمراد بالكبير في كلامهم هنا من يعبر عن نفسه، سواء كان بالغاً أو لا كما في النهاية . ثم اعلم أنه إنما يشهد بالملك لذي اليد بشرط أن لا يخبره عدلان بأنه لغيره فلو أخبراه لم تجز له الشهادة بالملك له كما في الخلاصة وقدمناه . وأشار المؤلف إلى أن القاضي لو رأى عيناً في يد رجل فإنه يجوز له القضاء بالملك له كما في الخلاصة والبزازية، وبه ظهر أن قول الشارح في تقرير أن الشاهد إذا فسر للقاضي أنه يشهد عن سماع أو معاينة يد لم يقبله أن القاضي لا يجوز له أن يحكم بسماع نفسه ولو تواتر عنده ولا برؤية نفسه في يد إنسان سهو إلا أن يحمل ما قالوا لو رأى شيئاً في يد إنسان ثم رآه في يد غيره فإنه لا ينتزعه منه من غيره أن يدعيه الأوّل، فما في الفتاوى فيما إذا ادعاه المالك وما في الشرح فيما إذا لم يدعه . قوله : (وإن فسر للقاضي أنه يشهد له بالتسامع أو بمعاينة اليد لا تقبل) وهذا هو الصحيح كما ذكره مسكين في شرحه لكنه استثنى الموت والموقف فتقبل، ولو فسر للقاضي أنه أخبره من يثق به واستثنى العمادي في الفصول الوقف فلو شهدا به وقالا نشهد بالتسامع تقبل لأن الشاهد ربما يكون عمره عشرين سنة وتاريخ الوقف مائة سنة فيتيقن القاضي أنه يشهد بالتسامع فالإفصاح كالسكوت إليه أشار ظهير الدين المرغيناني. وفي الخلاصة: لو شهدا عند القاضي أن فلاناً مات وقالا أخبرنا بذلك من نثق به جازت شهادتهما وهو الأصح، والخصاف أيضاً جوز ذلك وفيه اختلاف المشايخ ا هـ. ومعنى التفسير للقاضي أنه شهد بالتسامع أن يقولا شهدنا لأنا سمعنا من الناس، أما إذا قالا لم نعاين ذلك ولكنه اشتهر عندنا جازت ؛ كذا في الخلاصة والبزازية. وفي الينابيع تفسيره أن يقول في النكاح لم أحضر العقد وفي غيره أخبرني من أثق به أو سمعت ونحوه. وفي المحيط معزياً إلى المنتقى : إذا شهدوا أنه مات على هذه الدابة فهي ميراث، ولو شهدوا أن أبا هذا المدعي مات وهذه الدار يوم مات أو شهر مات أو سنة مات فهو جائز له ولو رآه على حمار يوماً لم يشهد أنه له لاحتمال أنه ركبه بالعارية، ولو رآه على حمار خمسين يوماً أو أكثر ووقع في قلبه أنه له وسعه أن يشهد أنه له لأن الظاهر أن الإنسان لا يركب دابة مدة كثيرة إلا بالملك ا هـ . وفي البزازية : عاين الشاهد دابة تتبع دابة وترضع له أن يشهد بالملك والنتاج. شهدا أن فلان بن فلان مات وترك هذه الدار ميراثاً ولم يدركا الميت فشهادتهما باطلة لأنهما شهدا بملك لم يعاينا سببه ولا رأياه في يد المدعي ا هـ. والله أعلم . ونحوه وفيه خلاف، فالمتون قاطبة قد أطلقت القول بأن الشاهد إذا فسر أنه يشهد بالسماع لا تقبل الرواية، وبه صرح كثير من علمائنا وعبارة قاضيخان ولو قالوا شهدنا بذلك لأنا سمعنا الناس لا تقبل شهادتهم .اهـ. قلت : وعبارة الخانية : إذا شهد الشهود بما تجوز به الشهادة بالسماع وقالوا شهدنا بذلك لأنا سمعنا من الناس لا تقبل شهادتهم .انتهت ثم نقل نحوه عن فتاوى شيخ الإسلام علي أفندي التركية وعربها ثم قال : فتحرر من النقول المعتبرة أن الشاهد في أصل الوقف إذا فسر إنه يشهد بالتسامع لا تقبل شهادته كما هو صريح المتون المتقدمة التي تمشي غالباً على ظاهر أصحابنا كما تقدم نقله عن الخيرية وما في التنوير تبعاً للدرر مستنداً في الدرر لما في العمادية وفي التنوير إلى الخلاصة قائلاً وهو الأصح . فذاك قول مخالف لما عليه المتون وكثير من أصحابنا على أنا نقابل ما في العمادية والخلاصة بما في الخانية من عدم قبوله لأن قاضيخان فقيه النفس كما صرح به في البحر من باب العيب وأنه يقتصر على الأشهر فكان المعتمد، وصرحوا بأن قاضيخان من أجل من يعتمد على تصحيحاته ويكفينا أنه ظاهر الرواية، وليس هذا في الوقف خاصة بل في جميع المواضع التي يجوز للشاهد الشهادة فيها بالتسامع، وأنت على علم بأن ما في المتون والشروح مقدم على ما في الفتاوى، وإنما أكثرت النقل في المسألة للاختلاف فيها لمحرره علي بن محمد التركماني غفر الله لهما وللمؤمنين .اهـ. ذكره في مجموعته الفقهية الكبرى ومن خطه نقلت
He testifies for him by hearsay or by seeing possession: it is not accepted. The two (the testifiers) repel the hand of the other from them, so evidence of ownership is lacking. And from Abu Hanifa: it is permissible for him to testify in these two cases as well, by analogy with garments, and the difference we have explained. And if the two are minors who cannot express themselves, like property that has no hand, then he may testify to ownership for those who have possession. According to this, the meaning of 'adult' in their speech here is one who can express himself, whether he is pubescent or not, as in al-Nihaya. Then know that he only testifies to ownership for the possessor on condition that two just men do not inform him that it belongs to another. If they inform him, then his testimony of ownership for him is not permissible, as in al-Khulasa and we have presented it. And the author indicated that if the judge sees an object in the hand of a man, it is permissible for him to judge ownership for him, as in al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyya. By this it becomes clear that the statement of the commentator in establishing that when the witness explains to the judge that he testifies by hearing or seeing a hand, it is not accepted, that the judge is not permitted to judge by his own hearing even if it is mutawatir, nor by his own seeing in the hand of a person, is an oversight, unless it is interpreted as what they said: if he saw something in the hand of a person then saw it in the hand of another, he does not take it away from him unless the first claims it. Thus what is in the fatwas is when the owner claims it, and what is in the commentary is when he does not claim it. His saying: (And if he explains to the judge that he testifies for him by hearsay or by seeing possession, it is not accepted) This is the correct view, as mentioned by Miskin in his commentary, but he excepted death and the place of standing (al-mawqif), so it is accepted. And if he explains to the judge that he was informed by someone he trusts, and al-Imadi in al-Fusul excepted endowment (waqf), so if they testify to it and say 'We testify by hearsay', it is accepted because the witness's age might be twenty years and the date of the endowment a hundred years, so the judge is certain that he testifies by hearsay, so disclosure is like silence, as indicated by Zahir al-Din al-Marghinani. And in al-Khulasa: if two testify before the judge that so-and-so died and say 'We were informed of that by someone we trust', their testimony is permissible, and it is the most correct; al-Khassaf also permitted it, and there is disagreement among the mashayikh. End. And the meaning of 'interpretation to the judge' that he testifies by hearsay is that they say 'We testify because we heard from people'. As for if they say 'We did not witness that but it became famous among us', it is permissible; similarly in al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyya. And in al-Yanabi', its interpretation is that in marriage he says 'I did not attend the contract' and in other matters 'someone I trust informed me' or 'I heard' and the like. And in al-Muhit, citing al-Muntaqa: if they testify that he died on this riding animal, then it is inheritance; and if they testify that the father of this claimant died and this house (was his) on the day he died or the month he died or the year he died, it is permissible for him. And if he saw him on a donkey for one day, he may not testify that it is his due to the possibility that he rode it as a loan. But if he saw him on a donkey for fifty days or more and it occurred in his heart that it is his, it is permissible for him to testify that it is his, because the apparent is that a person does not ride an animal for a long period except by ownership. End. And in al-Bazzaziyya: the witness saw an animal following an animal and suckling, he may testify to ownership and offspring. Two testified that so-and-so son of so-and-so died and left this house as inheritance, but they did not perceive the deceased, so their testimony is invalid because they testified to ownership whose cause they did not witness nor did they see it in the hand of the claimant. End. And Allah knows best. And similar to it, and there is disagreement in it. The texts (mutun) in general have stated fully that when the witness explains that he testifies by hearsay, the report is not accepted, and many of our scholars have stated this. And the expression of Qadikhan: if they say 'we testify to that because we heard people', their testimony is not accepted. End. I say: and the expression of al-Khaniyya: when the witnesses testify to what is permissible by hearsay testimony and say 'we testify to that because we heard from people', their testimony is not accepted. End. Then he transmitted similar from the fatwas of Shaykh al-Islam Ali Afandi al-Turki and its Arabic version, then he said: So it is established from reliable transmissions that the witness regarding the original endowment if he explains that he testifies by hearsay, his testimony is not accepted, as is explicit in the preceding texts which generally follow the apparent of our companions, as was transmitted from al-Khayriyya. And what is in al-Tanwir following al-Durar, relying in al-Durar on what is in al-Imadiyya and in al-Tanwir on al-Khulasa saying it is the most correct, that is a statement opposing what the texts and many of our companions are upon, for we counter what is in al-Imadiyya and al-Khulasa with what is in al-Khaniyya of its non-acceptance, because Qadikhan is a sagacious jurist, as stated in al-Bahr in the chapter of defect, and that he restricts himself to the most famous, so he is the relied upon. And they stated that Qadikhan is among those whose corrections are relied upon, and it suffices us that it is apparent from the narration. And this is not specific to endowment but in all places where hearsay testimony is permissible for the witness. And you know that what is in the texts and commentaries takes precedence over what is in the fatwas. I have transmitted copiously on the issue due to the disagreement in it, for its reviser Ali ibn Muhammad al-Turkmani, may Allah forgive him and the believers. End. He mentioned it in his major jurisprudential collection, and from his handwriting I transmitted.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with the ruling on testimony based on hearsay (tasamu') or seeing possession (mu'ayanat al-yad). The core rule is that such testimony is not accepted. The commentary explains the rationale: possession alone does not prove ownership. There is a narration from Abu Hanifa that allows testimony in these cases by analogy with garments, but the preferred view differs. The passage then discusses conditions: the witness may testify to ownership for the possessor only if no two just men inform him it belongs to another. It also discusses the judge's role: if the judge sees an object in someone's hand, he may judge ownership based on his own observation, but there is disagreement about the strength of such a judgment. The text then addresses the specific case when a witness explains to the judge that his testimony is based on hearsay. The correct view is that it is not accepted, with exceptions for death and the place of standing (al-mawqif). Al-Imadi excepted endowment (waqf) as well. The passage cites various sources like al-Khulasa, al-Bazzaziyya, and al-Yanabi' to illustrate different scenarios. It also discusses testimony regarding inheritance of property based on the death of the father, and testimony regarding ownership of an animal based on prolonged use. There is a significant intra-Hanafi dispute: many texts (mutun) and scholars like Qadikhan hold that if the witness explains that he testifies by hearsay, the testimony is not accepted. However, some later authorities like al-Imadi and al-Khulasa accept it in certain cases. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq sides with the majority view (the texts and Qadikhan), considering it more reliable and a matter of principle beyond just endowment. The commentary emphasizes that the texts and commentaries take precedence over fatwa collections.

Key Terms
تسامع (tasāmu'): Hearsay; testimony based on what one has heard from others, not on direct knowledge or observation.
معاينة اليد (mu'āyanat al-yad): Seeing possession; testifying that someone possesses an object based on having seen it in their hand, without direct knowledge of ownership.
تفسير للقاضي (tafsīr lil-qāḍī): The act of the witness explaining to the judge the basis of his testimony, e.g., that it is based on hearsay.
وقف (waqf): Endowment; a charitable trust where property is dedicated for religious or philanthropic purposes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a witness testifies that a property is an endowment (waqf) and explicitly says: 'I testify based on what I have heard from others'?
A) The testimony is accepted because it is about an endowment.
B) The testimony is not accepted because it is based on hearsay.
C) The testimony is accepted only if the witness is over fifty years old.
D) The testimony is accepted only if the judge already knows about the endowment.

Key Takeaway
Testimony must be based on direct knowledge; hearsay and mere possession are insufficient, and explicit hearsay disclosure invalidates the testimony in the mufta bihi Hanafi view, except in specific cases where the witness does not explicitly say 'I heard'.

Testimony of the Blind: Why It Is Not Accepted and When It May Be Executed
Ruling on blind testimony with qiyas proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of a blind person, explain the proof based on qiyas to hadd punishments, and identify the exception for hearsay matters.

Core Idea
A blind person's testimony is rejected due to lack of visual identification, akin to doubt (shubha) in hadd.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains why the Hanafi school generally rejects the testimony of a blind person. The author clarifies that 'non-acceptance' means the judge should not rely on it, but if he does, the judgement may be executed. We will explore the underlying analogy to hadd punishments and the nuance that blind persons can testify in matters based solely on hearing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The testimony of a blind person is not accepted (ghayr maqbul). This includes both pre- and post-acquisition blindness.
The ruling applies to the performance (ada') stage, not the bearing of testimony (tahammul).
2
Understand the proof: qiyas to hadd
Just as doubt (shubha) prevents execution of hadd, ambiguity in visual identification prevents accepting blind testimony.
The analogy is explicit in the text: 'And it becomes like hadd punishments and qisas.'
3
Note the distinction between acceptance and validity
Non-acceptance means the judge is not obliged to base judgement on it, but if he does, the judgement may be executed.
This is supported by the ruling from Khizanat al-Muftin.
4
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf holds that if blindness occurs after testimony but before judgement, the testimony can still be used. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) disagree.
Sadr al-Shari'a noted Abu Yusuf's view is 'more apparent', but the mufta bihi is the majority view.
5
Identify the exception for hearsay matters
Blind persons can testify in matters like lineage (nasab) where hearing suffices and sight is not required.
The text says: 'And it includes matters whose basis is hearsay, contrary to Abu Yusuf.'

يقال قبلت القول إذا حملته على الصدق كذا في المصباح. والمراد من يجب قبول شهادته على القاضي ومن لا يجب لا من يصح قبولها ومن لا يصح لأن من جملة ما ذكره ممن لا يقبل الفاسق وهو لو قضى بشهادته صح بخلاف العبد والصبي والزوجة والولد والأصل لكن في خزانة المفتين : إذا قضى بشهادة الأعمى أو المحدود في القذف إذا تاب أو بشهادة أحد الزوجين مع آخر لصاحبه أو بشهادة الولد لوالده أو عكسه نفذ حتى لا يجوز للثاني إبطاله وإن رأى بطلانه ا هـ . فالمراد من عدم القبول عدم حله وذكر في منية المفتي النفاذ بشهادة المحدود بعد التوبة قوله : (ولا تقبل شهادة (الأعمى لأن الأداء يفتقر إلى التمييز بالإشارة بين المشهود له والمشهود عليه ولا يميز الأعمى إلا بالنغمة وفيه شبهة يمكن التحرز عنها بجنس الشهود والنسبة لتعريف الغائب دون الحاضر وصار كالحدود والقصاص . فشمل الأعمى وقت الشهادة قبل التحمل أو بعده وما إذا . الأداء قبل القضاء لأن بعد عمي المراد بعدم قبولها عدم القضاء بها لأن قيام أهليتها شرط وقت القضاء لصيرورتها حجة عنده، وصار كما إذا خرس أو أو فسق بخلاف موت الشاهد وغيبته لأن الأهلية بالموت قد انتهت وبالغيبة ما بطلت؛ كذا في الهداية. وشمل ما كان طريقه السماع خلافاً لأبي :

قوله : (لكن الخ) أقول : لعل ما في الخزانة محمول على ما إذا كان القاضي يرى ذلك بقرينة قوله «حتى لا يجوز للثاني الخ ) تأمل قوله : (وذكر في منية المفتي الخ) أي في كتاب القضاء في بحث القضاء في المجتهد فيه ونصه : قضى بشهادة محدودين في قذف وهو لا يعلم بذلك ثم ظهر لا ينفذ قضاؤه وعليه أن يأخذ المال من المقضى له وكذا لو علم أنهما عبدان أو كافران أو أعميان، وقيل ينفذ فإنه ذكر إذا قضى بشهادة محدودين قد تابا ثم عزل أو مات ورفع ذلك إلى قاض آخر لا يراه أمضى القضاء الأوّل اهـ أقول وسيأتي بعد سبعة أوراق عدم نفاذ القضاء بشهادة العدو على عدوه. وهل يقال مثل ذلك في شهادة الأجير الخاص صارت واقعة الفتوى ولم أرها لأن العلة التهمة لا الفسق على ما يحرره المؤلف فيما سيأتي في شهادة العدو وهذه مثلها قوله : (أطلقه فشمل الأعمى وقت الشهادة الخ قال الرملي وقال أبو يوسف : إن عمي الأداء بعد القضاء يقضي بشهادته. قال في صدر الشريعة: وقوله أظهر قوله : وشمل ما كان طريقه السماع قال الرملي : أي كالنسب
Book of Testimonies. Chapter on whose testimony is accepted and whose is not. Chapter: The testimony of a blind person, a slave, and a child is not accepted unless they undertook (the testimony) while in slavery or childhood and then testified after liberation or adulthood. There is disagreement [regarding the meaning of 'acceptance']. It is said: 'I accepted the statement' means I considered it truthful, as in al-Misbah. What is meant is: whose testimony the judge must accept and whose he must not, not whose testimony is valid and whose is not, because among those mentioned as not accepted is the sinner (fasiq); if a judge passes a judgement based on his testimony, it is valid, unlike a slave, child, wife, or child [parent?] originally. However, in Khizanat al-Muftin: If a judge passes judgement based on the testimony of a blind person, or one who has been flogged for false accusation (mahrūm) after repentance, or one spouse with another for the other, or a child for a parent or vice versa, it is executed such that a second judge may not invalidate it even if he considers it void. End. So the meaning of non-acceptance is that it is not permissible. And it is mentioned in Munyat al-Mufti: Execution is valid with the testimony of a flogged person after repentance. His statement: (The testimony of) a blind person is not accepted because performance (ada') requires distinguishing by pointing between the person testifying for and the person testified against, and a blind person can only distinguish by voice, and there is ambiguity in that which can be avoided by the type of witnesses and lineage for identifying an absent person but not a present one; it is like the case of hadd punishments and qisas. This includes the blind at the time of giving testimony, whether before or after he became [blind?] or acquired [the knowledge?] ... [text unclear]... Because the capacity (ahliyya) is a condition at the time of judgement for it to be a proof according to him, and it becomes like the mute or a sinner, unlike the death or absence of a witness because capacity ends with death and is not invalidated by absence. Thus in al-Hidaya. And it includes matters whose basis is hearsay, contrary to Abu Yusuf... His statement: (But etc.) I say: Perhaps what is in al-Khizana is conditioned on when the judge holds that view, by the context of his statement 'such that a second may not invalidate it'... Reflect. His statement: (And it is mentioned in Munyat al-Mufti...) i.e., in the book of Judgement in the discussion of judgement for a mujtahid. Its text: He passed judgement based on the testimony of two who had been flogged for false accusation without knowing that, then it became apparent; his judgement is not executed, and he must take the money from the plaintiff. Similarly, if he knew they were slaves, disbelievers, or blind. And it was said that it is executed; he mentioned that if he passed judgement based on the testimony of two flogged people who had repented, then he was removed or died, and it was brought to another judge who does not hold that view, he confirms the earlier judgement. End. I say: It will come after seven pages that the judgement based on the testimony of an enemy against his enemy is not executed. Should the same be said regarding the testimony of a special employee (ajir khas)? The fatwa has occurred and I have not seen it because the cause is suspicion (tuhma) not sin (fisq), as the author will clarify later in the testimony of an enemy, and this is similar. His statement: (He made it absolute, so it includes the blind at the time of testimony...) al-Ramli said: And Abu Yusuf said: If blindness occurs after judgement, he should judge based on his testimony. Sadr al-Shari'a said: And his statement is more apparent. His statement: And it includes matters whose basis is hearsay; al-Ramli said: i.e., like lineage.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the chapter on whose testimony is accepted in the Hanafi school. The author defines 'acceptance' as the judge's obligation to admit and base judgement on testimony, not the validity of the testimony itself (since a sinful person's testimony is not accepted but if a judge bases judgement on it, it may still be executed). The main ruling: the testimony of a blind person is not accepted because performance requires visual identification. A blind person can only distinguish by voice, which is ambiguous. This is analogous to hadd punishments and qisas where similar precision is needed. The ruling covers blind at the time of testimony (whether before or after they became blind) and also if they became blind after acquiring knowledge but before giving testimony. The capacity (ahliyya) must exist at the time of judgement. Abu Yusuf differs: if a witness becomes blind after giving testimony but before judgement, the judgement may still be based on it. However, the relied-upon view is the general non-acceptance. The blind can still testify in matters based solely on hearing (like lineage) because sight is not necessary. The passage also touches on related issues like the testimony of a flogged person after repentance and the execution of judgements by a second judge. The text notes that a judge's judgement based on the testimony of those normally not accepted (like a blind person or a flogged person who repented) may still be executed and not revoked by another judge, highlighting the difference between acceptance (obligation to admit) and validity of judgement.

Key Terms
الأعمى (al-a‘mā): A blind person; one who cannot see.
الأداء (al-adā’): Performance; the act of giving testimony in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the testimony of a blind person generally not accepted?
A) Because blind people are unreliable.
B) Because they cannot distinguish between the parties by sight, creating ambiguity.
C) Because they are considered legally incapacitated.
D) Because they cannot write.

Key Takeaway
The testimony of a blind person is generally not accepted due to inability to visually identify parties, but an exception exists for matters based solely on hearing, and judges must be aware of the intra-Hanafi nuance regarding timing.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

Ruling on the Testimony of a Blind Person in Hanafi Law
Expansion on the ruling of blind testimony with rationale and disagreements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of a blind person, explain the legal reasoning (illa), and distinguish the positions of Abu Yusuf and Zufar on hearing-based matters.

Core Idea
A blind person's testimony is rejected due to the need for visual identification; voice alone is insufficient.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on the testimony of a blind person, as detailed in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The passage clarifies that 'non-acceptance' means the judge is not permitted to accept it, though if accepted, the ruling is enforceable. We will explore the rationale requiring visual distinction, the application to different timings of blindness, and the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding matters known by hearing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling on blind testimony
State the ruling that the testimony of a blind person is not accepted (ghayr maqbul). Understand that 'non-acceptance' means the judge is obligated not to accept it, but if he does, the judgment is enforceable.
This distinction is crucial: non-acceptance does not mean absolute invalidity.
2
Analyze the legal reason (illa)
The performance of testimony requires visual distinction (tamyīz bi-al-ishāra) between the claimant and defendant. A blind person can only distinguish by voice, which is insufficient and introduces suspicion (shubha).
This reasoning is analogized to hudud and qisas, where such testimony is also not accepted.
3
Examine timing of blindness
The ruling applies whether blindness occurs before or after hearing the testimony, because the capacity to perform is required at the time of judgment. This is unlike death or absence.
Abu Yusuf holds that if blindness occurs after judgment, the pre-blindness testimony can be accepted.
4
Explore the intra-Hanafi dispute on hearing-based matters
For matters known by hearing (e.g., lineage), Abu Yusuf and Zufar accept the testimony of a blind person, arguing that visual identification is not needed. The majority rejects this, maintaining the requirement.
Some later works (al-Khulasa, al-Nisab) choose the permissive view.
5
Consider broader implications
The author applies the same reasoning to a deaf-mute witness, indicating their testimony is also not accepted. This shows the principle's consistency.
The passage also discusses enforceability of judgments based on testimony of sinful persons, hadd-punished, etc.

باب من تقبل شهادته ومن لا تقبل
يقال قبلت القول إذا حملته على الصدق كذا في المصباح. والمراد من يجب قبول شهادته على القاضي ومن لا يجب لا من يصح قبولها ومن لا يصح لأن من جملة ما ذكره ممن لا يقبل الفاسق وهو لو قضى بشهادته صح بخلاف العبد والصبي والزوجة والولد والأصل لكن في خزانة المفتين : إذا قضى بشهادة الأعمى أو المحدود في القذف إذا تاب أو بشهادة أحد الزوجين مع آخر لصاحبه أو بشهادة الولد لوالده أو عكسه نفذ حتى لا يجوز للثاني إبطاله وإن رأى بطلانه ا هـ . فالمراد من عدم القبول عدم حله وذكر في منية المفتي النفاذ بشهادة المحدود بعد التوبة قوله : (ولا تقبل شهادة الأعمى) لأن الأداء يفتقر إلى التمييز بالإشارة بين المشهود له والمشهود عليه ولا يميز الأعمى إلا بالنغمة وفيه شبهة يمكن التحرز عنها بجنس الشهود والنسبة لتعريف الغائب دون الحاضر وصار كالحدود والقصاص . فشمل الأعمى وقت الشهادة قبل التحمل أو بعده وما إذا الأداء قبل القضاء لأن بعد العمى المراد بعدم قبولها عدم القضاء بها لأن قيام أهليتها شرط وقت القضاء لصيرورتها حجة عنده، وصار كما إذا خرس أو فسق بخلاف موت الشاهد وغيبته لأن الأهلية بالموت قد انتهت وبالغيبة ما بطلت؛ كذا في الهداية. وشمل ما كان طريقه السماع خلافاً لأبي يوسف
قوله : (لكن الخ) أقول : لعل ما في الخزانة محمول على ما إذا كان القاضي يرى ذلك بقرينة قوله «حتى لا يجوز للثاني الخ ) تأمل قوله : (وذكر في منية المفتي الخ) أي في كتاب القضاء في بحث القضاء في المجتهد فيه ونصه : قضى بشهادة محدودين في قذف وهو لا يعلم بذلك ثم ظهر لا ينفذ قضاؤه وعليه أن يأخذ المال من المقضى له وكذا لو علم أنهما عبدان أو كافران أو أعميان، وقيل ينفذ فإنه ذكر إذا قضى بشهادة محدودين قد تابا ثم عزل أو مات ورفع ذلك إلى قاض آخر لا يراه أمضى القضاء الأوّل اهـ أقول وسيأتي بعد سبعة أوراق عدم نفاذ القضاء بشهادة العدو على عدوه. وهل يقال مثل ذلك في شهادة الأجير الخاص صارت واقعة الفتوى ولم أرها لأن العلة التهمة لا الفسق على ما يحرره المؤلف فيما سيأتي في شهادة العدو وهذه مثلها قوله : (أطلقه فشمل الأعمى وقت الشهادة الخ قال الرملي وقال أبو يوسف : إن عمي الأداء بعد القضاء يقضي بشهادته. قال في صدر الشريعة: وقوله أظهر قوله : وشمل ما كان طريقه السماع قال الرملي : أي كالنسب

Chapter: Who's testimony is accepted and who is not. It is said: 'I accepted the statement' if I interpret it as truthful, as in al-Misbah. What is meant is who's testimony must be accepted by the judge and who must not, not who's testimony is valid and who is not, because among those mentioned as not accepted is the sinful person, and if the judge adjudicates based on his testimony it is valid, unlike the slave, minor, wife, and child, but in Khizanat al-Muftin: if he adjudicates based on the testimony of a blind person, or a hadd-punished person in qadhf if he repented, or based on the testimony of one of the spouses with another for their spouse, or based on the testimony of a child for their parent or vice versa, it is enforceable and cannot be overturned by a second judge even if he sees its invalidity. Thus what is meant by non-acceptance is that it is not permissible. And it is mentioned in Munyat al-Mufti that the testimony of a hadd-punished person after repentance is enforceable. His saying: (The testimony of the blind is not accepted) because the performance requires distinction by pointing between the claimant and the defendant, and the blind can only distinguish by voice, and there is suspicion that can be avoided by the type of witnesses and lineage to identify an absent person but not a present one, and it is like hudud and qisas. Thus it includes the blind at the time of testimony before hearing or after, and also when the performance is before judgment because after blindness, the meaning of non-acceptance is that judgment is not given based on it, because the establishment of its validity is a condition at the time of judgment for it to be a proof according to him, and it is like when he becomes dumb or sinful, unlike the death of the witness or his absence, because capacity ended with death and was not invalidated by absence; as in al-Hidayah. And it includes what is based on hearing, contrary to Abu Yusuf. His saying: (But etc.) I say: Perhaps what is in al-Khizana is based on the judge holding that opinion, indicated by his saying 'so it is not permissible for the second to invalidate it'. Consider. His saying: (And it is mentioned in Munyat al-Mufti etc.) i.e. in the book of Judgments in the discussion of judgment in ijtihad matters: He ruled based on the testimony of two hadd-punished persons in qadhf while not knowing that, then it became apparent that his judgment is not enforceable and he must take the money from the recipient, and similarly if he knew they were slaves, disbelievers, or blind, it is also unenforceable. And it is said it is enforceable, for it is mentioned that if he ruled based on the testimony of two hadd-punished persons who have repented, then he is removed or dies, and that is raised to another judge who does not hold that view, he enforces the first judgment. End. I say: It will come after seven folios the non-enforceability of judgment based on the testimony of an enemy against his enemy. And should the same be said regarding the testimony of a special employee? That has become a fatwa incident and I have not seen it, because the cause is suspicion, not sinfulness, as the author will explain later in the testimony of an enemy, and this is similar. His saying: (He made it absolute, thus it includes the blind at the time of testimony etc.) al-Ramli said: Abu Yusuf said: If blindness occurs after judgment, he should rule based on his testimony. He said in Sadr al-Shari'a: His statement is more apparent. His saying: (And it includes what is based on hearing) al-Ramli said: i.e. like lineage. As in Fath al-Qadir, and Zufar, and it is narrated from the Imam as in the commentary, and it is chosen in al-Khulasa and attributed to al-Nisab, definitively without mention of disagreement. And the author indicates the non-acceptance of the testimony of the deaf-mute by priority, whether by gesture or writing, and its completion is in the commentary of Ibn Wahban.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion upon the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, clarifying the rulings on the acceptance of testimony. The author begins with a crucial clarification: when the text says 'testimony is not accepted,' it means the judge is obligated not to accept it, not that it is inherently invalid. For example, a sinful person's testimony is not accepted, but if a judge does adjudicate based on it, the ruling is still enforceable and cannot be overturned by another judge. The same applies to a blind person, a hadd-punished person after repentance, or a spouse testifying for their partner. This is supported by references from Khizanat al-Muftin and Munyat al-Mufti. The main ruling discussed is the non-acceptance of the blind person's testimony. The reason ('illa) is that testimony requires visual distinction between the claimant and defendant; a blind person can only distinguish by voice, which is insufficient and introduces suspicion. This is analogous to hudud and qisas, where such testimony is not accepted. The rule applies regardless of when the blindness occurred, whether before or after hearing the testimony, because the capacity to testify is a condition at the time of judgment, not at the time of hearing. This is unlike the death or absence of the witness, which terminate or suspend capacity. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf holds that if the witness becomes blind after the judgment, his pre-blindness testimony can be accepted. Furthermore, for matters that can be known by hearing (like lineage), Abu Yusuf and Zufar accept the testimony of a blind person, and this opinion is chosen by some later authorities. The author also states that the deaf-mute's testimony is not accepted by priority (a fortiori), whether by gesture or writing. Overall, the Hanafi position is rejection of the blind's testimony, with a minority view accepting it for hearing-based matters.

Key Terms
الأعمى (al-a'mā): A person who is blind, both physically and in terms of being unable to see the parties in court.
المشهود له (al-mashhūd lahu): The person in whose favor the testimony is given (the claimant).
المشهود عليه (al-mashhūd 'alayhi): The person against whom the testimony is given (the defendant).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the legal reason (illa) for not accepting the testimony of a blind person?
A) Blindness is a sign of untrustworthiness.
B) Testimony requires visual identification between claimant and defendant.
C) The blind cannot write.
D) The blind are not allowed to testify in court.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school generally rejects blind testimony due to the need for visual identification, but permits it for hearing-based matters according to Abu Yusuf and Zufar.

Shahadat — Testimony
